Articles

Accutane (Isotretinoin)

Accutane (isotretinoin) is toxic and damages users for life. Other acne treatments include inclined bed therapy which is safe but only helps a little. Taking 750 mg/day of vitamin B5 (pantothenic acid) and 250 mg/day of carnatine is1 very effective but pantothenic acid can cause hair loss. This hair loss can usually be prevented with B vitamins and lysine.

Root causes of the damage from accutane include dysregulation of enzymes that maintain a healthy methylation status and shortening of telomeres. The dysregulation of enzymes can be partly reversed by taking2 lithium and getting3 more butyrate, which can done by taking sodium butyrate or eating more legumes. Supplements which support telomeres include Centella asiatica (Goto Kola), oleanolic acid, astragalus, and an oxidation resistant form of ascorbic acid, ascorbyl phosphate, also known as ascorbic acid 2-phosphate (ASC2P).

Toxicology

    Aluminium

    Aluminium (symbol Al; atomic weight 27.0), a metallic chemical element. Although never met with in the free state, aluminium is very widely distributed in combination, principally as silicates. The word is derived from the Lat. alumen (see ALUM), and is probably akin to the Gr. als (the root of salt, halogen, &c.). In 1722 F. Hoffmann announced the base of alum to be an individual substance; L. B. Guyton de Morveau suggested that this base should be called alumine, after Sel alumineux, the French name for alum; and about 1820 the word was changed into alumina. In 1760 the French chemist, T. Baron de Henouville, unsuccessfully attempted "to reduce the base of alum" to a metal, and shortly afterwards various other investigators essayed the problem in vain. In 1808 Sir Humphry Davy, fresh from the electrolytic isolation of potassium and sodium, attempted to decompose alumina by heating it with potash in a platinum crucible and submitting the mixture to a current of electricity; in 1809, with a more powerful battery, he raised iron wire to a red heat in contact with alumina, and obtained distinct evidence of the production of an iron-aluminium alloy. Naming the new metal in anticipation of its actual birth, he called it alumium; but for the sake of analogy he was soon persuaded to change the word to aluminum, in which form, alternately with aluminium, it occurs in chemical literature for some thirty years.

    Toxicology

    Aluminium is1 a neurotoxin, it is2 the primary cause of Alzheimer's disease. Aluminum also increases the chance of getting other neurological diseases including3 autism and attention deficit hyperactivity disorder (ADHD). Lysosomes are cytoplasmatic organelles which use to keep their interiors acidic, to break down garbage in the body which is then recyled or excreted. Aluminum inhibits4 lysosomal proton pumps, leading to the accumulation of cellular garbage in the body. Some of this garbage is flagged by the immune system as foreign material, so the immune system then attacks it, which can lead to autoimmune ailments. The garbage includes cholesterol containg lipid particles that are taken up into plaque, causing heart disease. Glutathione is a detoxifier and the body's master antioxidant. Aluminum decreases5 the regeneration of glutathione from the oxidized form by inhibiting NADP-isocitrate dehydrogenase, which supplies NADPH in mitochondria.

    Ailments

    • Brain - Dementia - Alzheimer's disease2
    • Brain - Neurodevelopmental disorder - Attention deficit/hyperactivity disorder (ADHD)3
    • Brain - Neurodevelopmental disorder - Autism3
    • Cardiovascular - Atherosclerotic plaque4
    • Immune dysfunction - Autoimmune disease4
    • Mitochondrial dsyfunction5

    Treatment

    Aluminium can be removed from the body with silica. Drinking silica water will remove aluminium, and silica water has no side effects. Aluminium can also be removed by silica rich supplements like horsetail and choline stabilized silica, but each of those can cause side effects.

    Malic acid, and some of its salts, including magnesium malate, also remove aluminum.

    Amygdalin

    Amygdalin is1 composed of glucose, benzaldehyde and hydrogen cyanide. Amygdalin has a bitter taste and is present in foods rich in nitrilosides. It is2 found in a high concentration in apricot kernels, in lower concentrations in nuts and the seeds and kernels of many fruits, and in still lower concentrations in many foods including lima beans, clover, and sorghum. In order to improve taste, the food industry has1 reduced the concentration of bitter substances like amygdalin by selection and cross-breeding, so people eating a modern diet are amygdalin deficient.

    The enzyme rhodanese converts3 the benzaldehyde and cyanide in amygdalin into the nutrients benzoic acid and thiocyanate. The enzyme beta-glucosidase releases the toxins benzaldahyde and cyanide in amygdalin. Healthy cells have a high concentration of rhodanase and a low concentration of beta-glucosidase, so they take only a little damage from amygdalin. Cancerous cells have a low concentration of rhodanase and a high concentration of beta-glucosidase, so they take enormous damage from amygdalin. Therefore taking a moderate amount of amygdalin will kill most cancer cells while not harming the healthy cells too much.

    Biology

    The amygdalin formula is laevo-D-mandelonitrile-B-D-glucoside-6-B-D-glucoside, a diglucoside with a cyanide radical. Laetrile is a decomposition product resulting from the hydrolysis of amygdalin. The laetrile formula is laevo-D-mandelonitrile-B-glucoronide. In 1949, Ernest T. Krebs, Jr. derived the name laetrile from the contraction of the chemical term lae vo-mandeloni trile. Krebs also designated laetrile as vitamin B17, but neither laetrile or amygdalin is a true vitamin, because they are not necessary for life. People can live without amygdalin or laetrile, they are just more likely to get cancer.

    History

    Amygdalin is among the most ancient nutrients used against cancer. Apricot kernels have been used since the days of the Chinese herbalist Pen T'sao in 2800 BC. Crystalline amygdalin was isolated in 1830 by two French chemists, Robiquet and Boutron. Amygdalin is found in bitter almonds and was named after the scientific name of the almond (Prunus Amygdalus).

    Treatment

    The amygdalin dose should4 start at one kernel and be increased increased one kernel at a time every few days until there are adverse effects, such as dizziness or headache. The typical final amygdalin dose is5 250 to 1,000 mg taken with a meal. Multiple doses per day are sometimes taken, and the total dose per day can be up to 4,000 mg, but more than 1,000 mg is never taken at any one time. Different apricot varieties have6 different amounts of amygdalin per seed. To get the correct dose, only use apricot seed packages which include the amygdalin content per seed or per gram.

    Amygdalin is3 very effective against adenocarcinoma, Hodgkin's disease, lymphomas, and cancers of the brain, breast, colon, liver, lung and prostate. It is moderately effective against other sarcomas and melanomas. It is poorly effective against leukemia. The higher the dose, the greater the effectiveness.

    Apigenin

    Apigenin, 4′,5,7-trihydroxy-flavone, isw a flavone, a type of flavonoid, which is a type of polyphenol, which is a type of phytochemical. Its molecular formula isa C15H10O5 and its molecular weight is 270 g/mol. Parsley and chamomile havew high concentrations of apigenin. Other sources include vine spinach, celery seed, green celery heart, Chinese celery, and dried oregano. The average dietary intake ranges from 0.45 mg/day in Australia to 4.2 mg/day in China. Apigenin is soluble in dimethyl sulfoxide (DMSO), but has low solubility in polar solvents such as water, and nonpolar solvents such as safflower oil.

    Apigenin is anticarcinogenic, antifungal, anti-inflammatory, antimutagenic, antioxidant, antiparasitic, anti-proliferative, and antiviral. Apigenin is also a reverse antibiotic (RA), which means it is ineffective against antibiotic susceptible bacteria but active against many antibiotic resistant bacteria. Apigenin inhibits many viruses including herpes simplex virus HSV-1 and HSV-2, hepatitis C virus, influenza virus, and African swine fever virus (ASFV). Apigenin inhibits hand, foot, and mouth disease (HFMD) caused by enterovirus 71 (EV71), but not that caused by coxsackievirus A16 (CAV16).

    Biology

    In nature, apigenin is typically found in a glycosylated form, with the core linked to a sugar moiety through hydroxyl groups (O-glycosides) or directly to carbon (C-glycosides). The common glycosides are apiin, apigenin-7-O-glucoside, apigenin-8-C-glucoside (vitexin), apigenin-6-C-glucoside (isovitexin), apigenin-7-O-neohesperidoside (rhoifolin), and apigenin-6-C-glucoside 8-C-arabinoside (schaftoside).

    Apigenin stopss the cell cycle at different proliferation stages including G1/S-phase or G2/M phase by modulating the expression of different cyclin-dependent kinases (CDKs) and other genes. Apigenin can regulate apoptotic pathways, changing mitochondrial membrane potential and causing the release of cytochrome C in the cytoplasm. In cancer cells, apigenin activates apoptosis by modulating Bcl-2, Bax, STAT-3 and Akt proteins expression. Apigenin crosses the blood‒brain barrier and inhibits monoamine oxidases (MAOs).

    Treatment

    A dose of about 200 mg isk non-sedative and 400 mg is very mildly sedative. The effect varies for different people and a person who wants to try apigenin should try the lower end of demonstrated effect (or even microdose to check for allergies) and then slowly step the dose up until the desired effect.

    • Bacterial infection - Antibiotic-resistant bacteria (Antibiotic resistant bacteria) (Reverse antibiotic) (RA)w
    • Brain - Dementia - Alzheimer's diseases
    • Brain - Neurosis - Depressions
    • Brain - Neurosis - Generalized anxiety disorder (GAD)s
    • Brain - Neurosis - Insomnias
    • Cancers w
    • Diabetes - Hyperglycemia (High blood sugar)s
    • Parasitic infection - Leishmaniasisw

    Arsenic

    Arsenic (symbol As, atomic weight 75.0), a chemical element, known to the ancients in the form of its sulphides. Aristotle gave them the name σανδαράκη, and Theophrastus mentions them under the name άρσϵνικόν. The oxide known as white arsenic is mentioned by the Greek alchemist Olympiodorus, who obtained it by roasting arsenic sulphide. These substances were all known to the later alchemists, who used minerals containing arsenic in order to give a white colour to copper. Albertus Magnus was the first to state that arsenic contained a metal like substance, although later writers considered it to be a bastard or semi metal, and frequently called it arsenicum rex. In 1733 G. Brandt showed that white arsenic was the calx of this element, and after the downfall of the phlogiston theory the views concerning the composition of white arsenic were identical with those which are now held, namely that it is an oxide of the element.

    Toxicology

    The commonest source of arsenical poisoning is the arsenious acid or white arsenic, which in one form is white and opaque, like flour, for which it has been mistaken with fatal results. Also, as it has little taste and no colour it is easily mixed with food for homicidal purposes. When combined with potash or soda it is used to saturate flypapers, and strong solutions can be obtained by soaking these in water; this fact has also been used with criminal intent. Copper arsenite (or Scheele's green) used to be much employed as a pigment for wallpapers and fabrics, and toxic effects have resulted from their use. Metallic arsenic is probably not poisonous, but as it usually becomes oxidized in the alimentary canal, the usual symptoms of arsenical poisoning follow its use.

    Acute

    In acute poisoning the interval between the reception of the poison and the onset of symptoms ranges from ten minutes, or even less, if a strong solution be taken on an empty stomach, to twelve or more hours if the drug be taken in solid form and the stomach be full of food. The usual period, however, is from half an hour to an hour. In a typical case a sensation of heat developing into a burning pain is felt in the throat and stomach. This is soon followed by uncontrollable vomiting, and a little later by severe purging, the stools being first of all faecal but later assuming a rice water appearance and often containing blood. The patient suffers from intense thirst, which cannot be relieved, as drinking is immediately followed by rejection of the swallowed fluid. There is profound collapse, the features are sunken, the skin moist and cyanosed. The pulse is feeble and irregular, and respiration is difficult. The pain in the stomach is persistent, and cramps in the calves of the legs add to the torture. Death may be preceded by coma, but consciousness is often maintained to the end. The similarity of the symptoms to those of cholera is very marked, but if the suspicion arises it can soon be cleared up by examining any of the secretions for arsenic. More rarely the poison seems to centre itself on the nerve centres, and gastrointestinal symptoms may be almost or quite absent. In such cases the acute collapse occurs in company with both superficial and deep anaesthesia of the limbs, and is soon followed by coma terminating in death. In criminal poisoning repeated doses are usually given, so that such cases may not be typical, but will present some of the aspects of acute and some of chronic arsenical poisoning. As regards treatment, the stomach must be washed out with warm water by means of a soft rubber tube, an emetic being also administered. Then, if available, freshly precipitated ferric hydrate must be given, which can be prepared by adding a solution of ammonia to one of iron perchloride. The precipitate is strained off, and the patient can swallow it suspended in water. While this is being obtained, magnesia, castor oil or olive oil can be given; or failing all these, copious draughts of water. The collapse must be treated with hot blankets and bottles, and subcutaneous injections of brandy, ether or strychnine. The pain can be lessened by injections of morphia.

    Chronic - Critical

    Arsenic may be gradually absorbed into the system in very small quantities over a prolonged period, the symptoms of chronic poisoning resulting. The commonest sources used to be wallpapers, fabrics, artificial flowers and toys: also certain trades, as in the manufacture of arsenical sheep dipping. But at the present time cases arising from these causes occur very rarely. In 1900 an outbreak of "peripheral neuritis" with various skin affections occurred in Lancashire, which was traced to beer made from glucose and invert sugar, in the preparation of which sulphuric acid contaminated with arsenic was said to have been used. But the nature of the disease in this case was decidedly obscure. The symptoms so closely resembled those of beriberi that it has also been suggested that the illness was the same, and was caused by the manufacture of the glucose from mouldy rice (see BERIBERI), though no proof of this was possible. The earliest symptoms are slight gastric disorders, loss of appetite and general malaise, followed later by colicky pains, irritation of eyelids and skin eruptions. But sooner or later peripheral neuritis develops, usually beginning with sensory disturbances, tingling, numbness, formication and occasionally cutaneous anaesthesia. Later the affected muscles become exquisitely tender, and then atrophy, while the knee-jerk or other reflex is lost. Pigmentation of the skin may occur in the later stages. Recovery is very slow, and in fatal cases death usually results from heart failure.

    Forensic Medicine

    After acute poisoning, the stomach at a post-mortem presents signs of intense inflammation, parts or the whole of its mucous membrane being of a colour varying from dark red to bright vermilion and often corrugated. Submucous haemorrhages are usually present, but perforation is rare. The rest of the alimentary canal exhibits inflammatory changes in a somewhat lesser degree. After chronic critical poisoning a widely spread fatty degeneration is present. Arsenic is found in almost every part of the body, but is retained in largest amount by the liver, secondly by the kidneys. After death from chronic poisoning it is found present even in the brain and spongy bone. The detection of arsenic in criminal cases is effected either by Reinsch's test or by Marsh's test, the urine being the secretion analysed when available. But Reinsch's test cannot be used satisfactorily for a quantitative determination, nor can it be used in the presence of chlorates or nitrates. And Marsh's test is very unmanageable with organic liquids on account of the uncontrollable frothing that takes place. But in such cases the organic matter can be first destroyed by one of the various methods, usually the moist method devised by Fresenius being chosen.

    Chronic

    Arsenic increases the risk of diabetes partly because of its propensity to form1 trivalent metabolites, which inhibit the synthesis of insulin.

    Arsenic increases2 generation of atherosclerotic plaque in the arteries, in part because of inflammation from reactive nitrogen species generation. The higher3 the exposure to arsenic, the thicker the Carotid intima-media thickness (cIMT), which is associated with arterial problems. Also, arsenic prolongs4 the QTc interval. Some water wells have high levels of arsenic.

    Ailments
    • Diabetes1
    • Cardiovascular - Atherosclerotic plaque2
    • Cardiovascular - Arterial wall thickening (Thickening of arterial walls)3
    • Heart - Long QT interval (Prolonged QTc interval)4

    Blackout Blinds

    In darkness, people produce1 melatonin. Melatonin lowers2 cortisol, glucose, blood pressure, and body temperature, all of which promotes sleep. Sleeping in the dark improves1 the quality and duration of sleep. Improved sleep leads to improved alertness, memory consolidation, problem solving ability, and emotional regulation.

    Nighttime light exposure, especially blue light, suppresses melatonin production, raises2 stress hormones and disrupts sleep patterns. Poor sleep causes health problems including inflammation, heart disease, insulin resistance and weight gain. It also increases3 the chance of getting breast cancer.

    Biology

    Light exposure, especially blue light, tells4 the suprachiasmatic nucleus (SCN) in the hypothalamus that it’s daytime and time to be alert. The SCN then sends signals to various parts of the body, influencing hormone production, body temperature, and other factors that affect our circadian rhythm (sleep-wake cycle).

    Sleep consists of several stages, including light sleep, deep sleep, and rapid eye movement (REM) sleep. Nighttime light exposure reduces the time spent in deep sleep and REM sleep, which are required for cognitive function and emotional regulation.

    Achieving Darkness

    Blackout curtains or blackout shades block out almost all light, creating a cave-like environment conducive to sleep. Blackout fabric for curtains is5 made of a tightly woven polyester or cotton and layered to the back of a cotton, suede, polyester, or velvet curtain. When buying blackout curtains, look4 for options that also provide insulation, which helps regulate room temperature for better sleep. A blackout liner for existing drapes blocks5 most light and could cost less than made to measure curtains.

    To achieve4 darkness, all devices with light emitting diode (LED) displays, such as alarm clocks or charging indicators should be removed or covered. The time on an LED alarm clock can be covered with black cardstock with a tape hinge on top taped to the clock so the cardstock can be lifted up to see the time. If a phone is used as an alarm, it can be placed face down. For those who rely on night lights for safety reasons, they should be red or amber instead of blue or white.

    Ailments

    Ailments caused by nighttime light exposure follow below.

    • Brain - Neurosis - Insomnia2
    • Cancer - Breast cancer3
    • Cardiovascular - Coronary artery disease6
    • Cardiovascular - Hypertension (High blood pressure)2
    • Cardiovascular - Stroke6
    • Diabetes - Low insulin sensitivity (Insulin resistance) (Low insulin response)2
    • Heart - Heart attack (Myocardial infarction) (MI)6
    • Heart - Atrial fibrillation6
    • Heart - Heart failure6
    • High stress hormone levels2
    • Obesity (Weight gain)2

    Budwig Protocol

    A cause of the cancer is1 lack of oxygen in cells, as discovered by Otto Warburg in 1931. Johanna Budwig developed paper chromatography in 1949 to identify fats. With this technique she proved that electron rich highly unsaturated linoleic (LA) and linolenic (LNA) fatty acids were the fats required to get oxygen into cells. Flaxseed oil is2 a good source of linoleic acid (LA) and3 the richest source of linolenic acid (LNA).

    Budwig observed4 that quark (a soft fresh cheese) contained the same sulphydryl groups found in cancer treatment drugs. These sulphydryl groups are cysteine and methionine amino acids. When the sulphydryl groups in low fat quark or cottage cheese react with the unsaturated fatty acids in flaxseed oil, the flaxseed becomes water soluble and enters cells to supply energy. Budwig found that with the improved cellular oxygen supply, her cancer patients found relief from all forms and stages of cancer including cancers of the gastrointestinal tract, brain, breast, and skin.

    Budwig also recommends5 a raw organic diet, mild exercise, flaxseed oil massage, regular sleep and adequate amounts of sunshine. She says that the environment should be as organic and natural as possible, homes should have woolen or silk carpets, there should be a lot of wood in home construction, and gemstones should be worn because they have good biological radiation. She rejects frozen food, preserved meat, bakery products, artificial electromagnetic fields (EMFs) (e.g. microwave and mobile phones etc.), synthetic textiles, and foam mattresses.

    Treatment

    The typical dose is 1 tablespoon of cold pressed flaxseed oil, 2 tablespoons of organic low fat cottage cheese or quark, and 2 tablespoons of either golden or brown flaxseeds for every 100 pounds of the person. The recipe which follows is for a 100 pound person, multiply the dose according to the weight of the person divided by 100 pounds.

    • Mix 1 tablespoon of flaxseed oil into a glass container
    • Mix in 2 tablespoons of cottage cheese or quark
    • Blend the mixture, preferably with an immersion blender, until a whipped cream consistency results
    • Grind 2 tablespoons of flax seeds in a coffee grinder until an airy, fluffy appearance results, usually in 1 minute
    • Place the ground flax seed in a separate glass or ceramic bowl
    • Add the cheese and oil mixture to the flax seed and stir with a spoon to combine
    • Optionally, add organic fruits, nuts, and spices for a tasty meal

    Barlean’s cold pressed flaxseed oil has no added lignins and comes in a dark bottle. Nancy’s organic low fat cottage cheese contains probiotics and enzymes, which even those with dairy sensitivities may tolerate. Quark is available in many European countries. Preservatives, hormones and protein degradation from high heat pasteurization in low quality cottage cheese prevents the water soluble flaxseed from being formed.

    Alternative Administration

    Some cancer patients can not eat or drink, in which case flaxseed oil should be blended6 with cottage cheese or quark, without any ground flax seeds. This blend can be applied by massage, and/or by covering the entire body in flaxseed blend and then wrapping the body in a natural cloth or sheepskin and have them sleep all night. The blend can also be administered in an enema.

    Ailments

    • Cancer1

    Cadmium

    Cadmium (symbol Cd, atomic weight 112.4 (O=16)), a metallic element, showing a close relationship to zinc, with which it is very frequently associated. It was discovered in 1817 by F. Stromeyer in a sample of zinc carbonate from which a specimen of zinc oxide was obtained, having a yellow colour, although quite free from iron; Stromeyer showing that this coloration was due to the presence of the oxide of a new metal. Simultaneously Hermann, a German chemical manufacturer, discovered the new metal in a specimen of zinc oxide which had been thought to contain arsenic, since it gave a yellow precipitate, in acid solution, on the addition of sulphuretted hydrogen. This supposition was shown to be incorrect, and the nature of the new element was ascertained.

    Toxicology

    Chronic

    Cardiomyocytes are the major type of cells that form the heart. Cadmium inhibits1 cardiomyocyte differentiation and cardiac induction, increasing the chance of congenital heart disease (CHD). Cadmium leads2 to peripheral artery disease.

    Cadmium is absorbed by tobacco plants, and that cadmium is part of the reason smoking leads to peripheral artery disease. Cadmium sources include3 mining, combustion emissions, and cadmium containing fertilizers. Cadmium is also incorporated into sulfides, carbonates, and phosphorites resulting in elevated cadmium concentrations in associated rock types. Weathering can lead to cadmium concentrations up to 5 mcg/L in soil water and up to 1 mcg/L in groundwater.

    Ailments
    • Cardiovascular - Peripheral artery disease (Peripheral arterial disease) (PAD) (Arterial insufficiency of the peripheral circulation)1
    • Heart - Congenital heart disease (CHD)1

    Calcium

    Calcium Orotate

    Treatment
    Ailments

    Hans Nieper used1 a dose of 600 mg/day to treat many ailments. The only side effects reported were a a loss of appetite among obese chronic overeaters, some of whom were able to lose weight. Calcium orotate has2 a bioavailability of at least 90%, while the next highest bioavailability is 45% for calcium aspartate. Because of this, a smaller amount of mineral is required in the supplement for the body to absorb the required dose, so adverse effects are minimized. Calcium orotate should treat every ailment that other calcium compounds treat with fewer adverse effects, but this has not been tested for most ailments because the other compounds are more popular.

    Copper Socks

    Copper socks (copper oxide socks, copper oxide impregnated socks), are socks woven with copper oxide impregnated fibers. Copper oxide is1 an antimicrobial and antifungal. Copper socks reduce bacterial and fungal foot odor. In a study, fifty six patients with athlete's foot (Tinea pedis) were given copper socks. In a 9 day average follow up, most patients had improvements or resolutions of scaling, erythema, fissuring, burning or itching, vesicular eruptions, edema, odor, and drainage.

    Ailments

    Ailments caused by bacterial and fungal foot infections follow below.

    • Body odor - Foot odor
    • Edema - Foot edema
    • Fungal infection - Foot - Athlete's foot (Tinea pedis)
    • Skin - Burning or itching
    • Skin - Erythema
    • Skin - Fissuring
    • Skin - Scaling
    • Skin - Vesicular eruptions (Vesicular rashes)

    Dimethylgycine (DMG)

    Dimethylgycine (DMG) is1 a tertiary amino acid, the dimethylated derivative of glycine. DMG is found in low levels in cereal grains, seeds, beans and liver. DMG reduces lactic acid buildup and improves endurance and recovery time from intensive exercise. DMG also helps with autism, epilepsy, and melanoma.

    Biology

    In the body, DMG is produced in the one-carbon transfer cycle from choline via betaine in an enzyme controlled transmethylation reaction. The liver converts DMG into other useful metabolites by oxidative demethylation. In this process, the two methyl groups of DMG can be made available for transmethylation reactions via sulfur-adenosylmethionine (SAMe). Dietary sources of active methyl groups include are choline, creatine and methionine. When these methyl donors fail to supply adequate methyl groups, supplemental DMG can provide methyl groups required for the detoxification of foreign substances and methylation of proteins, nucleic acids and biogenic amines.

    History

    Calcium pangamate was studied in the Soviet Union in the 1960s. At first it was thought to be a B vitamin, and called vitamin B15. Further research showed that it was not a true vitamin, and that it was the ester formed between DMG and calcium gluconate. In the digestive system, calcium pangamate is hydrolyzed to DMG, and DMG is the active compound in the body. For a while DMG was called vitamin B16, but further research showed it was also not a true vitamin.

    Treatment

    The typical treatment in studies is 125 mg twice per day, a total dose of 250 mg/day. The recommended daily dosage of DMG can range from 125 mg to over 1000 mg per day, depending on the area of use. If DMG is2 going to help a person, positive effects will be seen within four weeks. Recommended dosing of DMG for autism by weight follows below.

    Less than 20 kg125 mg/day
    20 to 30 kg250 mg/day
    30 to 45 kg375 mg/day
    45 to 60 kg500 mg/day
    More than 60 kg625 mg/day

    Ailments

    • Brain - Neurodevelopmental disorder - Autism3
    • Brain - Psychosis - Epilepsy4
    • Cancer - Melanoma1
    • Cancer - Metastatic cancer1
    • Cardiovascular - Angina (Angina pectoris) - Angina pain3
    • Cardiovascular - Hypertension (High blood pressure)1
    • Fibrosis5
    • Heart - Arrhythmias3
    • Hypoxia1
    • Immune dysfunction - Autoimmune disease - Lupus - Systemic lupus erythematosus (SLE)1
    • Lethargy1

    Improvements

    • Antibody response1
    • B and T cell function1
    • Cardiovascular - Coronary circulation1
    • Endurance1
    • Immune dysfunction1
    • Muscle recovery1
    • Oxygen utilization1

    Adverse Effects

    High dosages repeated over several days can6 cause irritability, insomnia, restlessness, and fast heart rate or heart rhythm disturbances. It is best to use a low dose, and if there are no adverse effects slowly increase the dose until there is a positive effect. If someone gets adverse effects then they should not use DMG.

    Dimethyl Sulfoxide (DMSO)

    Dimethyl sulfoxide (DMSO) ((CH3)2OS) is1 a sulfoxide (S=O) with two methyl groups (CH3). DMSO is an amphiphilic aprotic solvent. Its small size and amphiphilic nature allows it to diffuse between skin cells, carrying solutes through the skin. Because it carries most contaminants that are on the skin into the body, the skin must be perfectly clean before topical use. The area should be cleaned with a soap with few ingredients, and none of them should be synthetic. For example Kirk's Fragrance Free Traditional Castile Bar Soap2 has only sodium cocoate, water, glycerin, sodium chloride and sodium gluconate. After washing, the area should be3 air dried, because a towel might have a fragrance or another contaminant.

    DMSO does not dissolve polyethylene terephthalate (PETE), but it does dissolve many other types of plastics. Because even a PETE bottle could have traces of other chemicals, and DMSO will carry most contaminants through the skin, it should only be purchased if it comes in a glass bottle, and has a certificate of analysis showing that it is at least 99.99% pure. This is obtained by filtering DMSO through activated charcoal. Industrial grade DMSO must never be used by animals or humans.

    DMSO has4 very little odor, once inside the body, DMSO slowly breaks down by a reduction reaction, becoming dimethyl sulfide (DMS) ((CH3)2S2). Dimethyl sulfide has a sulfur based odor that is part of the odor from eating garlic, onions, and oysters. DMSO has a melting point of 18°C (65°F). Its expansion between the liquid and solid state is 230 times smaller than that of water, so it is safe to store in glass containers.

    DMSO was5 synthesized in 1866 by Alexander Saytzeff. DMSO is an intermediate product of the global sulfur cycle which distributes bioavailable sulfur. Its medical properties were discovered in 1963 by Stanley Jacob's research team. It is obtained industrially as a byproduct of the Kraft process (sulfate process) which converts wood into wood pulp.

    Biology

    DMSO is4 transdermal, easily penetrating the skin and blood–brain barrier. It carries many other drugs and supplements through the skin and blood-brain bariier, increasing their effects. It is antimicrobial with5 antibacterial, antiviral and antifungal properties. It increases4 production of white cells and macrophages.

    DMSO is a muscle relaxant and reduces inflammation and swelling by affecting inflammatory chemicals. It increases blood supply and delivery of oxygen to cells by dilating blood vessels and reducing blood viscosity. It has a calming effect on the central nervous system, it is an effective pain killer, blocking nerves conducting pain signals. It is antinociceptive, meaning that it reduces sensitivity to dangerous or harmful stimuli. It inhibits the cholinesterase enzyme from breaking down acetylcholine.

    DMSO is a metal detoxifier, binding to aluminum, mercury, cadmium, arsenic, and nickel and eliminating them through urination and sweating. It increases cell membrane permeability, allowing for removal of toxins. It is a diuretic. It is a potent free radical scavenger, and is radioprotective, reducing the mutagenic and damaging effects of x-rays and radiation therapy. It protects cells from mechanical damage. It is a cryoprotectant, used to protect stem cells, bone marrow cells, and organs from freezing damage during transportation.

    The half-life of DMSO in the human body is6 11 to 14 hours. It is primarily excreted through the kidneys, secondarily through the respiratory tract and bile.

    Treatment

    Once inside the body, DMSO breaks down, becoming dimethyl sulfide (DMS). The dimethyl sulfide smell is greater with oral administration than with other methods. Individuals metabolize DMSO differently depending on various factors, such as the water content of the body.

    Ear

    If there is an ear infection, DMSO is combined with an antibiotic or antiseptic. A recipe for ear infections is4 10% DMSO with 90% colloidal silver solution. One or two drops in each ear one to two times daily until three days after the symptoms disappear. Instead of colloidal silver, chlorine-dioxide/MMS can7 be used. Other antiseptics include hypochlorous acid and iodine.

    If there is4 no infection then a simple recipe is a 20% DMSO solution (DMSO diluted in distilled water or saline). One or two drops in each ear one to two times daily treats ear problems including tinnitus and hearing loss. The first time DMSO is tried in the ears, it should be diluted to 10% or less. For example, a 20% DMSO ear drop solution can be diluted with an equal amount of distilled water or saline to make it a 10% solution. If there is no pain, then the dilution can gradually be decreased until there is pain, in which case the dilution should be the lowest dilution before there was pain.

    Eye

    A simple recipe is5 a 25% DMSO solution (DMSO diluted in distilled water or saline). One drop of the solution once or twice per day treats eye problems, including cataracts and glaucoma. A DMSO solution of more than 50% should not be used on eyes because it will4 irritate the eye. The first time DMSO is tried on the eyes, it should be diluted to 20% or less. For example, a 25% DMSO eye drop solution can be diluted with an equal amount of distilled water or saline to make it a 12.5% solution. If there is no pain, then the dilution can gradually be decreased until there is pain, in which case the dilution should be the lowest dilution before there was pain.

    A three supplement recipe is8 a 30% DMSO solution, with 1.25% vitamin C and 1.25% glutathione. The DMSO dissolves the vitamin C and glutathione, and carries them into the eye, making this recipe more effective than DMSO alone. The first time this 30% DMSO solution is tried on the eyes it should be diluted with an equal amount of distilled water or saline to make it a 15% solution. If there is no pain, then the dilution can gradually be decreased until there is pain, in which case the dilution should be the lowest dilution before there was pain.

    Nasal

    A 10% DMSO solution (DMSO diluted in distilled water or saline) is4 often used with a neti pot or nasal tip applicator. For the nose, the DMSO concentration should not be higher than 20%. DMSO should not be used if the inside of the nose is raw or bleeding. The first time DMSO is tried in the nose, it should be diluted to 5% or less. For example, a 10% DMSO nasal solution can be diluted with an equal amount of distilled water or saline to make it a 5% solution. If there is no pain, then the dilution can gradually be decreased until there is pain, in which case the dilution should be the lowest dilution before there was pain.

    Nebulizing

    Rats who regularly breathed9 DMSO eventually developed toxicity. As a result, nebulizing is not recommended, however some individuals had a positive response to nebulized DMSO. Because DMSO dissolves many plastics, nebulizing should only be done with stainless steel and/or glass equipment.

    Oral

    A simple recipe is4 a 4% DMSO solution (DMSO diluted in distilled water or saline). An oral DMSO concentration should not be higher than 50%. The first time oral DMSO is tried, it should be diluted to 2% or less. For example, a 4% DMSO nasal solution can be diluted with an equal amount of distilled water or saline to make it a 2% solution. If there are no problems, then the dilution can gradually be decreased until there are problems, in which case the dilution should be the lowest dilution before there were problems.

    A common dose is five ounces (140 mL) of 4% DMSO, which is 140 * 0.04 = 5.6 mL, about 1 teaspoon of DMSO. The maximum 24 hour cumulative oral dose is8 1 ml/kg (about 1 teaspoon per 10 pounds).

    Topical

    Topical DMSO dries the skin, which causes irritation. Glycerin is a moisturizer and is10 safe in the body, it is even used intravenously, so it can be safely used with DMSO. Most other moisturizers, even plant based moisturisers, are composed of many compounds, which are not a problem topically but can be a problem when they cross the skin, so they should not be used with DMSO. Glycerin is more viscous than water, so it is easier to topically apply DMSO and glycerin than DMSO and water or DMSO and saline.

    To safely use4 DMSO topically, the application area must be clean, because DMSO carries most contaminants that are on the skin into the body. The area should be cleaned with a soap with few ingredients, and none of them should be synthetic. For example Kirk's Fragrance Free Traditional Castile Bar Soap2 has only sodium cocoate, water, glycerin, sodium chloride and sodium gluconate. After washing, the area should be3 air dried, because a towel might have a fragrance or another contaminant. If there is time, the patient should have a shower before applying DMSO, only using a fragrance free soap with few ingredients, none synthetic. When applying DMSO, no synthetic material should be used. Organic cotton is safe, for example organic cotton balls11 can be used, and whatever balls are used can be disposed of afterwards.

    If used4 on sensitive parts of the skin, like the face or the scalp, a 40% DMSO solution (DMSO diluted in glycerin, distilled water or saline) should be used. The first time DMSO is tried on a sensitive part like the face or scalp, it should be diluted to 20% or less. For example, a 40% DMSO solution can be diluted with an equal amount of glycerin, distilled water or saline to make it a 20% solution. If there is no pain, then the dilution can gradually be decreased until there is pain, in which case the dilution should be the lowest dilution before there was pain.

    For parts of the skin that are not sensitive, an 80% DMSO solution (DMSO diluted in glycerin, distilled water or saline) can be used. The first time DMSO is tried on non sensitive skin, it should be diluted to 40% or less. For example, an 80% DMSO solution can be diluted with an equal amount of glycerin, distilled water or saline to make it a 40% solution. If there is no pain, then the dilution can gradually be decreased until there is pain, in which case the dilution should be the lowest dilution before there was pain.

    Earthing

    Earthing, also known as grounding, means making electrical contact with the earth. This can be done directly by touching outdoor soil, for example by walking barefoot, or by sitting on the ground. It can also be done indirectly, by touching a mat connected by a conductor to the ground of the electrical system, or by wearing1 shoes with a conductor, usually in the ball of the sole, to provide an electrical connection to the ground. There are earthing mats for the floor, for desks, and for beds. Studies show2 that earthing improves sleep, reduces pain and soreness, increases femoral neck bone density, reduces fasting glucose, and decreases red blood cell (RBC) aggregation.

    Procedure

    The direct way of earthing is to go outside and touch the ground, but most of our time is spent indoors, so an earthing mat is necessary to get plenty of earthing. The easiest and least expensive way to start earthing indoors is with a desk earthing mat, around thirty centimeters wide and a meter long, to be placed on a desk used for typing or writing. A floor mat is useful only if someone is usually barefoot. A fitted earthing sheet is very effective because we spend so much time sleeping, however it is the largest and most expensive earthing product. Also a fitted earthing sheet is only conductive for a few years because even with regular washing eventually the silver threads get covered with skin oils.

    Convenience and EMF

    With an earthing fitted sheet, the sheet has to be unplugged and replugged every time it is washed. For convenience, two fitted sheets should be bought, the bottom one is plugged into the ground and the top one is fitted over the bottom one. Because the sheets are in contact, the top fitted sheet is still connected electrically to the ground even though it is not plugged in. It can be removed for washing without unplugging the bottom one, when it is put back on the bed it will still be earthed. This costs more but because you switch the earthing sheets once the top one loses some conductivity, the combination will last twice as long, so the cost per year would be the same. To block a varying Electromagnetic Field (EMF) you can buy a conductive flat sheet. This will form a partial Faraday cage, protecting your body from a varying EMF. If the fitted sheet is plugged in, the flat sheet will also be earthed when it is tucked under the fitted sheet. Since there is no body weight on the flat sheet, it will pick up less skin oil and will therefore last longer. Even though the combination of two earthed fitted sheets and one flat sheet costs more, because it lasts longer the cost per year is similar.

    Sleep and Chronic Pain

    Clinton Ober tested3 the effect of earthing for thirty days on sleep and pain. Time to fall asleep improved in 85% of the earthed subjects, and in 13% of the control subjects, a net improvement of 72%. The quality of sleep improved in 93% in the earthed subjects, and in 13% of the control subjects, a net improvement of 80%. Feeling rested on waking improved in 100% of the earthed subjects, and in 13% of the control subjects, a net improvement of 87%.

    Muscle stiffness and pain improved in 82% of the earthed subjects, and in none of the control subjects, a net improvement of 82%. Back and joint pain improved in 74% of the earthed subjects, and in none of the control subjects, a net improvement of 74%.

    Inflammation and Pain with Delayed-Onset Muscle Soreness (DOMS)

    Dick Brown measured4 48 markers over a 3-day post-test period. Of these markers, four changed more than 50%. These markers were the AM soreness scale, the PM soreness scale, creatine kinase, and glycerophosphorylcholine. The subjects completed the Visual Analogue Soreness Scale at 8 AM and 5:30 PM. By the end of the post-test period, the soreness at 8 AM (AM soreness scale) decreased 101% more in the earthed group than in the control group. By the end of the post-test period, the soreness at 5:30 PM (PM soreness scale) decreased 86% more in the earthed group than in the control group.

    Creatine kinase (CK) is a marker of muscular damage, by the end of the post-test period, it decreased 87% more in the earthed group than in the control group. Glycerophosphorylcholine (GPC) is a choline donor, it can increase acetylcholine levels in motor units, is essential in phospholipids, and is important in the release of human growth hormone. Glycerophosphorylcholine aids sarcoplasmic Ca2+ transport, and cognitive degeneration is delayed with GPC supplementation. GPC increased 68% more in the earthed group than in the control group.

    Osteoporosis and Glucose

    The femoral neck z-score is a measure of femoral neck bone density. The z-score is the number of standard deviations above average of the bone density, for someone of that age, sex and race. Renal calcium excretion is inversely correlated5 with femoral neck z-score, meaning the less calcium is excreted, the higher the bone density. Karol Sokal and Pawel Sokal found6 that earthing earthing during sleep reduces renal excretion of calcium from 2.14 to 1.12 mmol/8 hours.

    Patients with non-insulin-dependent diabetes mellitus (NIDDM) were divided into two groups. One group was earthed for three days. The fasting glucose concentration of the ungrounded group decreased from 10.8 to 10.6 mmol/L, an improvement of 0.2 mmol/L. The glucose concentration in the earthed group decreased from 10.6 to 7.4 mmol/L, an improvement of 3.2 mmol/L, which was 3 mmol/L better than the ungrounded group.

    Red Blood Cell Aggregation

    Red blood cell aggregation increases7 the viscosity of blood. This leads to less blood flow, especially in the capillaries. That in turn leads to lower oxygenation and/or more work for the heart to pump the blood. This in turn leads to cardiovascular problems, especially hypertension. Gaétan Chevalier counted8 the number of large aggregates (4 or more blood cells clumped together) in earthed and ungrounded subjects. Before earthing, subjects had 35% of their blood cells in large aggregates, after two hours of earthing, subjects had 15% of their blood cells in large aggregates.

    Ailments

    Ailments caused by lack of earthing follow below.

    • Bone - Osteoporosis5 6
    • Brain - Neurosis - Insomnia3
    • Cardiovascular - Hypertension (High blood pressure)7
    • Diabetes - Hyperglycemia (High blood sugar)6
    • Musculoskeletal - Delayed-onset muscle soreness (DOMS)4
    • Musculoskeletal - Muscle stiffness3
    • Pain - Chronic pain3

    Ear Irrigator

    A low pressure ear irrigator cleans and unblocks the ear with a low risk of injury. Q-tips (cotton-tip applicator (CTA)) injure1 children at a rate of about 18/year per 100,000. Severe CTA injuries can result in tympanic membrane perforation (TMP), ossicular dislocation (joints between malleus-incus-stapes, or stapes footplate subluxation), hearing loss (conductive, sensorineural, or mixed), perilymphatic fistula, and facial nerve paralysis.

    An ear irrigator should have a blunt tip nozzle with spray holes around the end, so that it doesn't spray water straight into the delicate tympanic membrane. It should also have a water bottle with a lever to manually power and control the water flow. Water bottles with just a button for pumping take too much effort to pump water. Electric irrigators can spray with too high a pressure, and because they are not manual, if you feel the pressure is too high you have to let go of a button, which takes some time by which point the tympanic membrane could be perforated. With manual pumping, you stop putting pressure on the lever, which is a bit faster. An irrigator kit should come with a catch basin with a loop to go over the ear, to catch the water flowing out of the ear without using an extra hand to hold the basin. The Medi Grade Ear Washer Bottle2 has all these features.

    Water for the irrigator should be3 around body temperature, otherwise it can cause dizziness and lead to the eyes moving in a fast, side-to-side manner due to acoustic nerve stimulation. Water that is too hot can also burn the eardrum. The irrigator bottle should be4 filled with 1/4 of 3% hydrogen peroxide and the rest water, which results in a 0.75% hydrogen peroxide solution. The peroxide prevents infection and it slowly breaks down the wax. If there is an infection, use hypochlorous acid to treat the infection. Before irrigation, the ear canal should be inspected with an ear camera or otoscope.

    If the ear irrigation does not work on the first try, you can pour5 3% hydrogen peroxide into empty bottle with an eyedropper. Then pour a few drops to a dropperful into your ear, and leave it there for at least 20 minutes, then irrigate again. You can repeat this cycle daily. If this does not work after two weeks, see a Ear Nose Throat (ENT) doctor.

    Adverse Effects

    Adverse effects follow6 below.

    • Damage to the ear and eardrum (including perforation)
    • Ear wax being pushed into the ear by the water from the irrigator
    • Faintness or dizziness if the water is not at body temperature, from the caloric effect
    • Hearing loss and tinnitus
    • Infection of the porous bone surrounding the ear (mastoiditis)
    • Outer ear canal infection (e.g. otitis externa)

    Contraindications

    • Ear surgery within the last 18 months
    • Foreign object inside the ear canal
    • Outer ear canal infection (otitis externa) or middle-ear infection in the last 6 weeks
    • Perforated eardrum, tympanostomy tube (grommet, myringotomy tube), mastoid cavity, cleft palate in the last 12 months

    Ailments

    Ailments caused7 by ear blockages follow below.

    • Ear - Dizziness
    • Ear - Drainage from ear
    • Ear - Earache
    • Ear - Itching
    • Ear - Odor coming from the ear
    • Ear - Pain in the ear
    • Ear - Sudden or partial hearing impairment
    • Ear - Tinnitus (Ringing in the ear)
    • Ear - Vertigo

    Fenbendazole

    Fenbendazole is1 an antiparasitic with2 the formula C15H13N3O2S. Fenbendazole can be bought as a powder, or as the active ingredient in trademarked products including Phenbendazole, Panacur and SafeGuard. Fenbendazole is not water soluble and will be poorly absorbed unless taken3 with fats. Fenbendazole starts decomposing4 at 179°C.

    A scientist at Merck Animal Health was2 injecting different types of cancers into different mice body parts. The mice had parasites, and in order to eliminate the parasites she gave5 them fenbendazole. Those mice were cured of their cancer. The scientist was later diagnosed with stage 4 brain cancer and was given2 three months to live. She tried fenbendazole, and was cured after six weeks.

    Joe Tippens had cancer in the lung, neck, stomach, liver, bladder, pancreas and tail bone. He was given three months to live. In January 2017, after hearing3 the story of the scientist who cured her cancer with fenbendazole, Joe decided try fenbendazole plus cannabidiol (CBD) oil, curcumin, and vitamin E, thus creating the original Joe Tippens Protocol.

    Treatment

    The starting dose is2 222 mg/day, taken for three consecutive days each week. The heavier the person and the more severe the ailment, the more they should take. There is a fenbendazole dose guide6 for cancer and parasites. Fenbendazole can2 be taken up to one gram/day, up to 6 days per week. For cancer, if it does not shrink on the starting dose, gradually increase the dose up to 1 g/day 6 days per week until there are adverse effects, then go back to the last dose without the adverse effects. For parasites, follow the dosing on the fenbendazole dose guide6.

    If it taken as a powder, to increase3 absorption it should be mixed into a fat. The fat should be solid at room temperature so that the fenbendazole powder does not settle down to the bottom, as it would in a liquid. The solid fat should have a naturally long shelf life. Solid fats with long shelf life include coconut oil, and ghee. For an even longer shelf life, the fat should be from a glass jar. The amount of coconut oil or ghee to put7 on toast ranges from 5 to 15 grams, for an average of 10 grams. The concentration of 222 mg of fenbendazole in 10 grams of fat is 0.222 / 10 = 0.0222 (2.22%). The concentration of 444 mg in 10 grams is 4.44%.

    Flexbar

    Tennis elbow, or chronic lateral epicondylosis, is1 characterized by pain at the lateral epicondyle, aggravated by resisted muscle contraction of the carpi radialis brevis. Isolated eccentric training effectively treats chronic lateral epicondylosis, and this can be done at home using a flexible rubber bar (Flexbar) which is twisted using wrist flexion of the uninvolved limb and slowly allowed to untwist with eccentric wrist extension by the involved limb.

    Twenty one patients with chronic unilateral lateral epicondylosis were divided into a Flexbar group with 11 people and a standard treatment group with 10 people. The Disability of Arm, Shoulder, and Hand Questionnaire (DASH) was used to determine the disability. Pain was assessed using a Visual Analog Scale (VAS). Wrist extension and middle finger extension strength were measured bilaterally with a hand held dynamometer (Lafayette Manual Muscle Tester). Tenderness was assessed using a probe attached to the dynamometer.

    DASH scores improved by 76% in the Flexbar group versus 13% in the standard treatment group. VAS improved by 81% in the Flexbar group versus 22% in the standard treatment group. The combined strength deficit for wrist and middle finger extension improved by 79% in the Flexbar group versus 15% in the standard treatment group. The tenderness deficit improved by 71% in the Flexbar group versus 5% in the standard treatment group.

    Gc Protein-derived Macrophage Activating Factor (GcMAF)

    Serum α-N-acetylgalactosaminidase (nagalase) activity is high in people with cancer, autism, diabetes, immune disorders, viral infections and bacterial infections. The activity of nagalase correlates with the severity of the illness. Giving heterogenous cancer patients GC protein-derived macrophage-activating factor (GcMAF) decreased1 nagalase activity and improved clinical conditions. When autistic patients were given GcMAF, their nagalase declined2 and about 85% had improvements in language or socialization or cognition.

    Health

    Cancer

    Twenty patients with different types of neoplasms at different stages of malignant progression were given1 weekly administrations of 100 ng GcMaf. This was done for an average of 37 weeks. The nagalse levels were 2.84 nM/min/mg at the beginning, and fell to 1.59 nM/min/mg by the end. Many patients had clinical improvements.

    Sixteen nonanemic prostate cancer patients received3 14 to 25 weekly administrations of 100 ng GcMAF. Afterwards the serum nagalase levels decreased to those of healthy control values. No recurrence occurred for 7 years.

    Eight nonanemic colorectal cancer patients who had previously received tumor-resection but still carried tumor cells were given4 32 to 50 weekly administrations of 100 ng GcMAF. Afterwards nagalase levels decreased to normal. According to annual Computerized Axial Tomography (CT) scans, for the next 7 years there was no recurrence.

    Sixteen nonanemic metastatic breast cancer patients received5 16 to 22 weekly administrations of 100 ng GcMAF. Afterwards nagalase levels decreased to normal. There was no recurrence for more than 4 years.

    Autism

    Forty patients with autism were given2 weekly administrations of 100 ng GcMaf. The nagalse levels were 1.93 nM/min/mg at the beginning, and after an average of 14 injections, fell to 1.03 nM/min/mg by the end. On the improved Clinical Global Impression Scale (iCGI), about 85% of patients had improvements in language or socialization or cognition. Patients improved by an average of 2.98, on this scale 3 is a moderate improvement.

    Treatment

    GcMAF is available as an injection, a sublingual spray, a cream, an enteric capsule, and in yogurt. The yogurt can be made at home with a starter culture. The studies have been done with GcMAF injections. Bioavailability is high with injections, but injections have some risk and they are unpleasant. There is little independent information on the bioavailability of GcMAF in other forms. The bioavailability of GcMAF in the form of a cream and enteric capsule depend on the manufacturer, and the manufacturers are not disclosing their formulations on their web sites. The bioavailability of GcMAF from yogurt depends on the person, when they eat and how long since their last meal, so there is a wide variation. The sublingual spray carrier is just saline, without additives to increase absorption, so the bioavailability won't vary depending on an unknown formulation. Therefore if someone does not want an injection, and can afford the sublingual spray, they should use the spray. If they can not afford the spray, they should get a starter culture, make their own yogurt with it, and hope for the best.

    Ailments

    • Brain - Neurodevelopmental disorder - Autism2
    • Cancer1
    • Cancer - Breast cancer5

    Glutathione

    The tripeptide glutathione (γ-l-glutamyl-l-cysteinyl-glycine, GSH), is1 an antioxidant and reducing agent. It is required to regulate disulfide bonds of proteins, and dispose of electrophiles and oxidants. It mediates many physiologic reactions including metabolism of xenobiotics, and cellular signaling (cell-cycle regulation, proliferation, and apoptosis). Glutathione also maintains2 mitochondrial DNA (mtDNA), transports mercury out of cells, and protects against alcohol and persistent organic pollutants (POPs). Glutathione deficiency can be caused by alcohol, cadmium, neurodegenerative disorders, or chemical toxins including persistent organic pollutants (POPs) the primary source of which are conventionally grown foods.

    Biology

    Glutathione levels can be increased3 by its rate-limiting precursors glycine and cysteine. Cysteine has a low bioavailability, the best way of increasing the amount of cysteine in the body is to take N-acetyl cysteine (NAC). Supplementing with oral glutathione has low effectiveness because it is degraded by digestive peptidases. The degradation can be avoided by using sublingual, liposomal, or intravenous forms, but they are less convenient than oral glycine or NAC. Alpha-lipoic acid helps regenerate endogenous antioxidants such as glutathione. Selenium is a cofactor of glutathione peroxidase, selenium supplementation increases the expression and activity of some glutathione-related enzymes. Vitamin B2 (riboflavin) is a coenzyme for glutathione reductase, which converts oxidized glutathione into its reduced form. Vitamin B5 (pantothenic acid) helps support glutathione synthesis through its role in ATP production. Vitamin B12 (cobalamin) deficiency is associated with lower glutathione levels. For people with a vitamin C deficiency, supplementing vitamin C raises glutathione levels. For people with diabetes, supplementing vitamin E raises glutathione levels. Glutathione requires4 magnesium for its synthesis.

    Treatment

    The easiest way to treat a glutathione deficiency is to take glycine or N-acetylcysteine (NAC). Taking both, either with separate supplements or a glynac (a mixture of glycine and NAC) supplement raises levels even more, providing many benefits. A study found5 that glynac improved cognition, strength, gait‐speed, exercise capacity and other attributes and biomarkers. For epileptics, glycine sometimes reduces6 the number of seizures, NAC attenuates aminophylline-induced seizures but aggravates7 absence seizures. So epileptics and others with hyperexcitable neurons should take a double dose of glycine instead of glynac or glycine and NAC separately. To boost glutathione levels further, a multivitamin with organic magnesium should be taken, multivitamins which have magnesium in the form of magnesium oxide should never be taken because magnesium oxide has a low bioavailability. To boost glutathione levels even further, a vitamin B supplement should be taken. The B6 part of the supplement should preferably have regular niacin, not a time release form of niacin, like niacinamide or inositol hexanicotinate, because they might cause liver damage when used for a long time. The B9 part of the vitamin B supplement should be L-methylfolate (L-5-MTHF, (6S)-5-Methyltetrahydrofolic acid, Metafolin), not folic acid. The B12 part of the vitamin B supplement should be methylcobalamin and/or adenosylcobalamin (adenosyl B12, cobamamide, cobinamide). Hydroxocobalamin is unhealthy because it suppresses nitric oxide (NO). Cyanocobalamin depletes8 glutathione, might cause cyanide toxicity and should never be taken.

    Glutathione is2 required for many purposes, especially detoxification. Some ailments which glytathione deficiency contribute to follow below.

    • Brain - Dementia - Alzheimer's disease

    Glycine

    Glycine, also known as amino acetic acid, is1 the smallest amino acid (with a molecular weight of 75.067 g/mol). Its name is derived from the Greek word glykys, meaning sweet. Glycine is synthesized by the body from serine, choline, threonine, and glyoxylate. Glycine was isolated in 1820 from the acid hydrolysis of gelatin. Glycine is2 a biosynthetic precursor for porphyrins, purines, creatine, sarcosine, bile salts, and glutathione. It is one third of collagen and elastin. Gelatin is3 made by boiling animal bones, cartilage, and connective tissues, and is the richest source of glycine, about 19 g glycine/100g. Ground beef has about 2 g glycine/100g. Meat is a good source of glycine, vegans are usually glycine deficient.

    Biology

    Glycine is1 in the hydrophilic and hydrophobic parts of the polypeptide chain. It is involved as antacid and with tissue restoration (scar formation). It is a regulator of growth hormone (GH) synthesis, gene expression, and protein activity. Glycine is a neurotransmitter and inhibits different brain regions. In the central nervous system (CNS), glycine binds to chloride-sensitive ion channels to inhibit postsynaptic neurons. Inhibiting glycinergic signaling evokes pain hypersensitivity. It inhibits2 protein glycation, and increases hepatic production of pyruvate, a hydrogen peroxide scavenger.

    While the body synthesizes glycine, extra glycine is needed from diet for optimal health. In young men the glycine flux is 35 mg/kg/h in the fed state, during the post-absorptive state, the flux is halved to 18 mg/kg/h, giving a necessary dietary intake of 1.5 to 3 g/day. The rate of synthesis is estimated at 12 to 15 mg/kg/h. Glycine is abundant in plasma and represents 11.5% of the amino acids and 20% of the nitrogen in body proteins. Plasma concentration ranges from 200 to 300 mol/L.

    Treatment

    Supplementation of 3 g/day of glycine helps4 with many problems. More glycine, up to the deficiency of about 0.14 g/kg/day (10 g/day for a 70 kg person) may help5 more.

    Deficiency

    Glycine inhibits postsynaptic neurons and is required for the synthesis of collagen and glutathione. Some ailments which glycine deficiency contribute to follow below.

    Ailments

    • Arthritis - Osteoarthritis5
    • Bladder - Bladder dysfunction6
    • Bone - Low bone mineral density (Low BMD)7
    • Brain - Neurodevelopmental disorder - Attention deficit/hyperactivity disorder (ADHD)8
    • Brain - Neurosis - Deviant behavior6
    • Brain - Neurosis - Insomnia9
    • Brain - Neurosis - Obsessive-compulsive disorder (OCD) (Obsessive compulsive neurosis) (Obsessives)10
    • Brain - Psychosis - Epilepsy6
    • Brain - Psychosis - Schizophrenia11
    • Diabetes - Low insulin sensitivity (Insulin resistance) (Low insulin response)12
    • Glycation13
    • Metabolic syndrome14
    • Speech disorders6
    • Vascular disorders - Vegeto-vascular dystonia (VVD) (Vegetative-vascular disorders)6

    Hypochlorous Acid

    Hypochlorous acid (HOCl) (perchloric acid) (hydrogen hypochlorite) (chlorine hydroxide) is1 an oxyacid of chlorine. It is a strong oxidizer and a weak acid. It partially dissociates into hypochlorite ions (CLO-) and protons (H+). Hypochlorous acid exists only as an aqueous solution because it is in equilibrium with the anhydride. Hypochlorous acid reacts with a base to form a hypochlorite salt, like sodium hypochlorite (NaOCl) in bleach.

    A hypochlorous acid solution is2 stable when the pH is between 3.5 and 5.5. If the solution gets too acidic, it partially dissociates into chlorine gas. If it gets too alkaline, it partially converts into hypochlorite.

    Disinfectant

    Myeloperoxidase (MPO) is3 used by neutrophils and monocytes to react hydrogen peroxide and chlorine to produce hypochlorous acid. Hypochlorous acid kills4 bacteria, fungus and viruses, and it deactivates prions and amyloid seeds. It is safe for disinfecting surfaces. The hypochlorite ions (CLO-) disinfect5 and are known as the available free chlorine (AFC) in the solution. The AFC decreases when hypochlorous acid is exposed to UV radiation, sunlight, air or when the temperature is greater than 25°C. Hypochlorous acid should be stored in sealed containers in cool, dark places. It can be applied to the skin or mucus membranes with low risk of irritation.

    When hypochlorous acid is aerosolized, some of chlorine evaporates, increasing the pH by approximately 1.3. So to produce a hypochlorous acid aerosol, the PH of the solution should be reduced to its lower stable limit of 3.5 before spraying, so that the aerosol PH is 3.5 + 1.3 = 4.8, which is within the stable PH range.

    Bleach is6 an aqueous solution of hypochlorous acid and sodium hypochlorite. At low PH, the proportion of hypochlorous acid is high and the proportion of sodium hypochlorite is low. At high PH, the proportion of sodium hypochlorite is high and the proportion of hypochlorous acid is low. The PH of bleach is high, between 8 and 13. Most of the germ killing properties of bleach come from the presence of the hypochlorous acid, even though bleach has a low proportion of hypochlorous acid, that small amount of hypochlorous acid is killing most of the germs. The high proportion of sodium hypochlorite irritates any skin it contacts, but is only killing a small portion the germs.

    Production

    Hypochlorous acid can7 be produced at home by electrolysing salt water at a PH of 3.5 to 5.5. The electrodes should not be made out of an alloy that contains chromium, like stainless steel, because that could8 form hexavalent chromium. Safe metals for the electrode include titanium and iridium. The Eco One Electrolyzed Water System - Portable Hypochlorous Acid (HOCl) Generator9 from Ecoloxtech has a titanium electrode. The water should be distilled. The salt should be pure, non-iodized with no anti-caking agents. Sea salt should not be used because it contains minerals which will form many compounds during the electrolysis process. To reduce the PH, use distilled white vinegar or food grade vinegar without additives.

    Hypochlorous acid can1 also be produced by bubbling chlorine gas in water.

    Adverse Effects

    Hypochlorous acid at concentrations as10 high as 500 ppm in mouthwash have been tested on human subjects with no adverse effects. Hypochlorous acid at a concentration of 5 ppm in drinking water was tested on mice for twelve weeks with no adverse effects.

    Inclined Bed Therapy

    Inclined bed therapy (IBT) was popularized1 by Andrew K. Fletcher. Some Egyptians slept on inclined beds, and some of those beds had an elevation of 6 inches. Studies show that inclined bed therapy reduces acid reflux, blood sugar, sleep apnea, and snoring. Infants younger than three years old should not be on inclined beds because they can accidentally roll2 from supine to prone and suffocate.

    Procedure

    A bed with feet can be inclined by putting bed risers, also called furniture risers, below the feet at the head of the bed. If the head of the bed has a bar instead of feet, then extruded closed cell foam can be cut to size and placed under the bar. Foam is good because it won't scratch the floor, extruded foam should be used instead of expanded foam because it's stronger. If it is a storage bed without feet, then a bed size foam wedge can be placed underneath the mattress.

    The elevation in most studies is around 7 inches. This high elevation requires a bed with a footboard, otherwise the mattress will slide down. If the bed does not have a footboard, the elevation should only be two inches. This will have less benefits than a high elevation bed, but it is easier to get used to, and it's still better than a level bed. Even if the bed has a footboard, if the person can not sleep well with a high elevation, then the elevation should be lowered until the person does sleep well.

    Acid Reflux

    Acid reflux occurs when the stomach stays open and gastric acid flows back into the esophagus. Acid reflux happens less often when upright or inclined because gravity pulls the acid down.

    Bashir Ahmad Khan tested3 the effect raising the head of the bed 8 inches for one week on symptoms of gastroesophageal reflux. The supine reflex time proportion decreased from 15.0% to 13.7%, the acid clearance time decreased from 3.8 minutes to 3.0 minutes, the number of refluxes 5 min longer decreased from 3.3 to 1.0, and the symptom score decreased from 2.3 to 1.5. Sleep disturbances improved in 65% of patients.

    Blood Sugar

    Erica Billen and Tetaake Yee Ting measured4 the Random Blood Sugar (RBS) of seven individuals. They started with the head of the bed raised by 4 inches, then after several weeks, increased the height to 6 inches. After about 8 weeks, the average RBS decreased by 16%.

    Sleep Apnea

    Obstructive sleep apnea (OSA) is characterized by an obstruction of the upper airway during sleep. Fábio Fabrício found5 that a 7.5° incline decreased the apnea-hypopnea index (AHI) from 15.7 to 10.7 events/hour, and increased minimum oxygen saturation from 83.5% to 87%.

    Snoring

    Elisabeth Wilhelm found6 that increasing the inclination of the bed reduced snoring. A 10% inclination reducing snoring by 22% and a 20% inclination reduced snoring by 67%. Even a 10% inclination is high and can reduce the quality of sleep. Assuming a geometric reduction in snoring for an increase in inclination, then snoring decreases by inclination to the power of 1.6 = ln(67 / 22) / ln(20 / 10), and a reasonable inclination of 7.5% would reduce snoring by roughly 14% = 22% x (7.5 / 10) ^ 1.6.

    Treatment

    There are anecdotal reports from Earth Clinic7 and Inclined Bed Therapy8 that inclined bed therapy helps with ailments which follow below.

    Ailments

    • Arthritis
    • Back - Back pain
    • Brain - Dementia - Alzheimer's disease
    • Brain - Migraine
    • Brain - Neurosis - Insomnia
    • Brain - Parkinson's disease
    • Brain - Psychosis - Epilepsy
    • Cardiovascular - Hypertension (High blood pressure)
    • Cardiovascular - Poor circulation
    • Cellulite
    • Diabetes - Hyperglycemia (High blood sugar)
    • Edema
    • Eye - Glaucoma
    • Face - Acne
    • Fatigue
    • Functional somatic syndrome (FSS) - Fibromyalgia
    • Gastrointestinal disorder - Acid reflux
    • Gastrointestinal disorder - Heartburn (Acid indigestion) (Pyrosis) (Cardialgia)
    • Gastrointestinal disorder - Indigestion
    • Immune dysfunction - Autoimmune disease - Hashimoto's thyroiditis (Hashimoto's disease) (Chronic lymphocytic thyroiditis) (Autoimmune thyroiditis)
    • Lymph nodes - Swollen lymph nodes
    • Musculoskeletal - Muscle cramps
    • Neurodegenerative disease - Multiple sclerosis (MS)
    • Nose - Sinusitis
    • Reproductive disorder - Infertility
    • Respiratory disease - Asthma
    • Skin - Skin conditions
    • Skin - Varicose veins - Spider veins
    • Sleep disorder - Sleep apnea
    • Sleep disorder - Snoring
    • Urination - Nighttime urination

    Recoveries

    Intravenous Fluid

    Intravenous fluids (IV fluids), were invented in England to treat dehydration. Latta developed a salt water solution to treat cholera, which kills by dehydration. His solution was sodium chloride and water. By 1885, Sidney Ringer determined that a solution perfusing a heart must contain sodium, potassium and calcium salts to keep it beating.

    Ringer's Solution

    Ringer's solution usually contains sodium chloride, potassium chloride, calcium chloride, and sodium bicarbonate. In the 1930s Alexis Hartmann added sodium lactate to form Ringer's lactate solution. Conservatively, perioperative mortality could be reduced by 7% if a balanced solution like Ringer's solution was used instead of normal saline.

    Blood Plasma

    The plasma is a solution in water of a varied number of substances, and as a solvent it confers on the blood its power of acting as a carrier of food stuffs and waste products. One important food substance, oxygen, is, however, only partly carried in solution, being mainly combined with haemoglobin in the red corpuscles. The food stuffs carried by the plasma are proteins, carbohydrates, salts and water. The main waste products dissolved in it are ammonium carbonate, urea, urates, xanthin bases, creatin and small amounts of other nitrogenous bodies, carbonic acid as carbonates, other carbon compounds such as cholesterin, lecithin and a number of other substances. Mammalian blood plasma has the following approximate composition:

    Perioperative Mortality

    Normal saline is a version of Latta's solution. It only has sodium chloride and water. Its concentration of sodium and chloride is higher than in blood. In 2012 Andrew Shaw found that patients who received saline during surgery had a mortality rate of 5.6%, and patients who received a calcium-free physiologically balanced crystalloid solution had a mortality rate of 2.9%. Using a balanced solution would have avoided 48% = 100% - 100% x 2.9 / 5.6 of the deaths.

    In 2018 Matthew W. Semler found that patients who received saline during surgery had a mortality rate of 11.1%, and patients who received a balanced crystalloid solution had a mortality rate of 10.3%. Using a balanced solution would have avoided 7% ~ 7.2% = 100% - 100% x 10.3 / 11.1 of the deaths.

    About 4.2 million people die from surgery each year. For a conservative estimate, the lower mortality avoidance percentage from Semler's study of 7% is used. If surgeons used balanced solutions worldwide, about 300,000 lives per year would be saved (7.2% of 4.2 million).

    Bibliography

    1. Andrew D. Shaw et al., Major complications, mortality, and resource utilization after open abdominal surgery: 0.9% saline compared to Plasma-Lyte (May 2012)
    2. Matthew W. Semler et al., Balanced Crystalloids versus Saline in Critically Ill Adults (Feb 2018)
    3. Dmitri Nepogodiev et al., Global burden of postoperative death (Feb 2019)

    Ionic Toothbrush

    Teeth have1 a negative charge and plaque particles have a positive charge. The positively charged plaque particles are attracted to the negatively charged teeth and stick there. An ionic toothbrush has2 at least one positively charged pad on the handle that the person contacts, and a negatively charged rod that extends toward the brush and contacts the saliva of the mouth. This gives the person, including their teeth, a positive charge. The plaque particles are then repelled from the teeth and attracted to the negatively charged rod. This leads to a reduction in plaque and gingival inflammation and bleeding.

    For the electrical circuit to be completed, the skin touching a positive pad has to be wet and the negative rod has to be wet. A tiny amount of current from a battery or solar panel keeps the rod and pads charged.

    Solar Ionic Toothbrush

    Solar panels on a3 solar ionic toothbrush provide sufficient current in a lit bathroom to charge the rod and pads. If someone has large hands they can cover all the solar panels, so they should hold the toothbrush in a way that keeps at least one solar panel uncovered. The power is on as long as the toothbrush is in a lit location, so there is no power button. Solar panels can last for decades so there are no electrical parts to replace. The brush head is removable and has to be replaced when it wears out.

    Battery Ionic Toothbrush

    With a battery ionic toothbrush, the battery typically lasts for several months. Once it dies, you have to buy another toothbrush.

    Ailments

    • Mouth - Gingival inflammation and bleeding2
    • Mouth - Plaque2
