    Tucker Protocol

    Eli Jordon Tucker found1 that dimethyl sulfoxide (DMSO) and hematoxylin cured cancer. Tucker was2 an orthopedic surgeon who pioneered many orthopedic techniques, including discovering how to graft bones from one species to another. Tucker’s bone research required purchasing cattle and he noticed that many of the cows had cancers covering their faces. Tucker wondered if there was a cancer antibody in those cows, so he administered extracts of their blood into lab rats and mice and observed anticancer activity for certain cancers. To study the cancer, Tucker looked for a dye to stain tumors, and realized hematein (oxidized hematoxylin) was the perfect dye because it stained the cancers one color and normal cells another color.

    However, hematoxylin has poor solubility in some laboratory solvents, so it was of limited use. Tucker tried dimethyl sulfoxide (DMSO) once it came into use around 1963 and discovered it could dissolve a large amount of hematoxylin (1 L of DMSO can dissolve 400 g of hematoxylin). He also found there was a "marked increase in central necrosis of the neoplasm" indicating this mixture could eliminate cancers while sparing normal cells.

    Tucker then conducted toxicity studies, initially in dogs, where he found intravenous DMSO mixed with hematoxylin had about one quarter of the toxicity of intravenous DMSO alone. Intravenous DMSO is only toxic at high concentrations, primarily because of osmotic injury. When DMSO-hematoxylin is placed into the blood, it will oxidize and turn into DMSO-hematein, which has a different color. DMSO-hematein does not accumulate in non-cancerous tissue. The only physiologic change he observed from DMSO-hematein was blood urea nitrogen dropping by around 50%, indicating the mixture improved kidney function.

    He then began treating spontaneous cancers in animals, which included terminal cases with massive tumors. In all of these cases, there was a prompt response, and the animal subsequently recovered. He told his associates of his findings, and was approached by a colleague who had a comatose female patient dying from inoperable fibrosarcoma. As she was his first human patient, Tucker gave her a slow infusion, and over weeks of treatment, the tumor gradually receded until it was small enough to remove, and she had a full recovery.

    Following this, he treated numerous patients, but had to stop curing patients in the United States because the FDA banned DMSO research in 1965. So he conducted a small trial in Panama with a colleague and got his cases published in 1968. In 1971 the American Cancer Society published a bulletin stating DMSO-hematoxylin was an unproven remedy. Tucker received pushback from some of his colleagues for using DMSO-hematoxylin and was expelled from the staffs of two hospitals for administering the treatment so he never published anything further about it.

    Jim McCann learned about DMSO-hematoxylin through Tucker’s 1968 paper, and tried to get ahold of hematoxylin but was unable to at that time as access was restricted. Eventually, in 1985 he was able to get hematoxylin, and used it on a prostate cancer patient on the verge of death, resulting in a full recovery. Then he treated about five other people in Canada, received pushback, and in 1995 moved to Riobamba, Ecuador. He cured cancer patients with DMSO-hematoxylin, and cured stroke and heart conditions with DMSO and chelation therapies like EDTA. Doctors began seeking him out, and he trained around 20 doctors. The doctors he trained educated others in turn, and roughly 100 doctors began using DMSO-hematoxylin.

    When exposed to air hematoxylin becomes hematein. Hematoxylin has no anticancer effects, it is hematein which kills the cancer. DMSO-hematoxylin has been successfully used intravenously, orally, intralesionally, intra-arterially, rectally, and topically. However, there has not been any success when injected into the tumor, this may be because there is insufficient oxygen in the tumor to convert inactive DMSO-hematoxylin into anticancerous DMSO-hematein.

    DMSO

    Dimethyl sulfoxide (DMSO) ((CH3)2OS) is3 a sulfoxide (S=O) with two methyl groups (CH3). DMSO is an amphiphilic aprotic solvent. Its small size and amphiphilic nature allows it to diffuse between skin cells, carrying solutes through the skin. Because it carries most contaminants that are on the skin, the skin must be perfectly clean before topical use. The area should be cleaned with a fragrance free soap with few ingredients, and none of them should be synthetic. For example Kirk's Fragrance Free Traditional Castile Bar Soap4 has only sodium cocoate, water, glycerin, sodium chloride and sodium gluconate. After washing, the area should be5 air dried, because a towel might have a fragrance or another contaminant.

    DMSO is6 odorless, the garlic-like body odor and taste in the mouth that some experience is from the metabolite dimethyl sulfide (DMS) ((CH3)2S2), part of onion and garlic flavors. Its melting point is7 18°C (65°F). Its expansion between the liquid and solid state is 230 times smaller than that of water, so it is safe to store in glass containers. It does not dissolve polyethylene terephthalate (PETE), but it does dissolve many other types of plastics. Because even a PETE bottle could have traces of other compounds, and DMSO will carry most contaminants through the skin, it should only be purchased if it comes in a glass bottle, and has a certificate of analysis showing that it is at least 99.99% pure. DMSO is hygroscopic, so an open container of DMSO will absorb water from the air.

    Hematoxylin

    Haematoxylum is8 a genus of flowering plants in the family Fabaceae. It is native to the Americas. The genus name is derived from the Greek words haema, meaning blood because the heartwood is dark red, and toxon, meaning bow because the plant’s wood is used to make archery bows.

    Hematoxylin (C16H14O6) is1 extracted from the Haematoxylum campechianum (Palo de Campeche) tree in the state of Campeche in Mexico. This colorless substance oxidizes when exposed to the air, becoming2 hematein which has a bright red color. Hematein is8 used as a dye for textiles, ink, and1 a histology dye. A histology dye stains tissues, making cellular components visible under a microscope. Hematein attaches to acidic cell structures, and since cancer cells are acidic, it preferentially stains cancer cells, making them easier to distinguish under a microscope. The hematein in turn slowly oxidizes9 further to form trioxyhaematein, which is unusable for staining purposes. Hematoxylin is very soluble in ethyl alcohol and in hot water. Hematein only slightly so. Hematoxylin staining solutions are in reality hematein solutions with slowly decreasing hematein content. The expression "hematoxylin staining solution" is incorrect, but is still in use for historical reasons.

    Hematoxylin has10 been used as an astringent for the treatment of diarrhea and in the treatment of urinary infections because of the presence of the dye which is excreted in urine. The dose ranged from 0.6 to 2 grams.

    Treatment

    DMSO-Hematoxylin Mixture Recipe

    Dissolve1 25 g of hematoxylin in 75 mL of DMSO, and stir until no sediment settles at the bottom. Put this DMSO-hematoxylin mixture in a dark glass bottle.

    Oral Administration

    Warning: Do not use oral dosing of DMSO-hematoxylin if the patient has1 stomach cancer, because if you drink DMSO-hematoxylin the stomach tumor will disappear too quickly, leaving a hole in the stomach. Always treat stomach cancer intravenously or topically.

    Use 1 mL of DMSO-hematoxylin with 60 mL of distilled water per 75 lbs (34 kg) of body weight. So if the person weighs 150 lbs (68 kg), they should use 2 mL of DMSO-hematoxylin with 120 mL of distilled water. Drink it on an empty stomach, at least two hours away from food.

    People take7 up to a teaspoon (5 mL) of DMSO orally, and rats tolerate10 four times as much DMSO-hematoxylin as DMSO. If DMSO-hematoxylin is at least as safe as DMSO for humans, than an oral dose of 5 mL for a 150 lb (68 kg) person, or 2.5 mL of DMSO-hematoxylin per 75 lbs (34 kg) of body weight would be safe. The higher the dose the faster the cancer is killed. If the cancer is severe, it is probably worth trying a dose up to 2.5 mL of DMSO-hematoxylin with 150 mL of distilled water per 75 lbs (34 kg) of body weight.

    Topical Application

    The initial dose is1 1 mL of the DMSO-Hematoxylin Mixture per 75 lbs (34 kg) of body weight, with an equal amount of glycerin, distilled water or saline. The cancer area should be cleaned with a fragrance free soap with few ingredients, and none of them should be synthetic. For example Kirk's Fragrance Free Traditional Castile Bar Soap4 has only sodium cocoate, water, glycerin, sodium chloride and sodium gluconate. After washing, the area should be5 air dried, because a towel might have a fragrance or another contaminant. When applying this aqueous mixture, no synthetic material should be used. Organic cotton is safe, for example organic cotton balls11 can be used, and whatever balls are used can be disposed of afterwards. With organic cotton balls, or organic cotton swabs, or fingers cleaned with a fragrance free soap, apply this aqueous mixture on the cancer, twice a day. If the cancer is in an inacessible location, apply it on a large area of skin like the stomach or legs, because the mixture will get into the blood and kill cancer throughout the body. There is a higher concentration of the mixture where it is applied and so it will kill cancer at a high rate in that area, the concentration in the rest of the body will be lower so it will kill the cancer else in the rest of the body at a lower rate. DMSO is7 absorbed within ten minutes, but its opening of the skin barrier persists for up to three hours. In that time, don't go swimming, and if you spill anything on yourself, immediately wash it off with water, preferably distilled water.

    People take7 up to two tablespoons (30 mL) of 50% DMSO solution topically, which is one tablespoon (15 mL) of DMSO. Rats tolerate10 four times as much DMSO-hematoxylin as DMSO. If DMSO-hematoxylin is at least as safe as DMSO for humans, than a topical dose of 15 mL for a 150 lb (68 kg) person, or 7.5 mL of DMSO-hematoxylin per 75 lbs (34 kg) of body weight would be safe. The higher the dose the faster the cancer is killed. If the cancer is severe, it is probably worth trying a topical dose up to 7.5 mL of DMSO-hematoxylin per 75 lbs (34 kg) of body weight.

    Intravenous Administration

    The first treatment should be 0.5 mL of DMSO-hematoxylin added to a 250 mL infusion bottle of 5% glucose. Set the drop rate at less than 50 drops/minute to avoid irritating the blood vessels. If there are no adverse effects, increase the dose to 1 mL per 75 lbs (34 kg) of body weight.

    Turpentine

    Turpentine (in M. Eng. turbentine, adapted through the O. Fr. turbentine or terebentine from Lat. terebinthina, sc. resina, resin of the terebinth, Gr. τερέβινθος or τέρυινθος, the oleo-resins which exude from certain trees, especially from some conifers — such as Pinus syhestris — and from the terebinth tree, Pistacia lerebinthus, L. It was to the product of the latter, now known as Chian turpentine, that the term was first applied. The terebinth tree and its resin were well known and highly prized from the earliest times. The tree is a native of the islands and shores of the Mediterranean, passing eastward into Central Asia; but the resinous exudation found in commerce is collected in the island of Chios. Chian turpentine is a tenacious semi-fluid transparent body, yellow to dull brown in colour, with an agreeable resinous odour and little taste. On exposure to the air it becomes dry, hard and brittle. In their natural characters, turpentines are soft solids or semi-fluid bodies, consisting of resins dissolved in turpentine oil, the chief constituent of which is pinene. They are largely used in the arts, being separated by distillation into rosin or colophony (see ROSIN), and oil or spirit of turpentine.

    Crude or Common Turpentine

    Crude or common turpentine is the commercial name which embraces the oleo-resin yielded by several coniferous trees, both European and American. The principal European product, sometimes distinguished as Bordeaux turpentine, is obtained from the cluster pine, Pinus Pinaster, in the Landes department of France. Crude turpentine is further yielded by the Scotch fir, P. Sylvestris, throughout northern Europe, and by the Corsican pine, P. Laricio, in Austria and Corsica. In the United States the turpentine yielding pines are the swamp pine, P. australis, and the loblolly, P. Taeda, both inhabiting North and South Carolina, Georgia and Alabama. Venice turpentine is yielded by the larch tree, Larix europaea, from which it is collected principally in Tirol. Strassburg turpentine is obtained from the bark of the silver fir; but it is collected only in small quantities. Less known turpentines are obtained from the mountain pine, P. Pumilio, the stone pine, P. Cembra, the Aleppo pine, P. halepensis, &c. The so-called Canada balsam, from Abies balsamea, is also a true turpentine.

    Oil of Turpentine, or Turps

    Oil of Turpentine, or Turps, as a commercial product is obtained from all or any of these oleo-resins, but on a large scale only from crude or common turpentine. The essential oil is rectified by redistillation with water and alkaline carbonates, and the water which the oil carries over with it is removed by a further distillation over calcium chloride. Oil of turpentine is a colourless liquid of oily consistence, with a strong characteristic odour and a hot disagreeable taste. It begins to boil at about 155°C., and its specific gravity is between 0.860 and 0.880. It rotates the plane of polarized light both to right and left in varying degrees according to its sources, the American product being dextrorotatory and the French laevorotatory. It is almost insoluble in water, is miscible with absolute alcohol and ether, and dissolves sulphur, phosphorus, resins and caoutchouc. On exposure to the air it dries to a solid resin, and absorbing oxygen gives off ozone — a reaction utilized in the disinfectant called "Sanitas." Agitated with successive quantities of sulphuric acid and distilled in a current of steam, it yields terebene, a mixture of dipentene and terpinene mainly, which is used in medicine. Chemically, oil of turpentine is a more or less complex mixture of hydrocarbons generically named terpenes. Oil of turpentine is largely used in the preparation of varnishes and as a medium by painters in their "flat" colours.

    Pharmacology and Therapeutics

    Oil of turpentine (Oleum terebinthinae) is administered internally as an anthelmintic to kill tapeworm. Applied externally it possesses, in higher degree than any of its fellows; the properties of the volatile oils. It acts as a rubefacient, an irritant and a counter-irritant. It is also an antiseptic and, in small quantities, a feeble anaesthetic. It is absorbed by the unbroken skin. The drug is largely employed as a counter-irritant, the pharmacopoeial liniments being very useful applications. Such conditions as myalgia, bronchitis, "chronic rheumatism" and pleurisy are often relieved by its use. It may also be employed as a parasiticide in ringworm and similar conditions.

    In large doses oil of turpentine causes purging and may induce much haemorrhage from the bowel; it should be combined with some trustworthy aperient, such as castor oil, when given as an anthelmintic. It is readily absorbed unchanged and has a marked contractile action upon the blood vessels. This gives it the rare and valuable property of a remote haemostatic, erroneously supposed to be possessed by so many useless drugs. It must not be used to check haemorrhage from the kidneys (naematuria) owing to its irritant action on those organs, but in haemoptysis (haemorrhage from the lungs) it is often an invaluable remedy. In large doses it has a depressant action on the nervous system, leading even to coma and total abolition of reflex action. The drug is excreted partly by the bronchi — which it tends to disinfect — and partly in the urine, which it causes to smell of violets. Glycuronic acid also appears in the urine. A small portion of the drug is removed by the skin, in which it may give rise to an erythematous rash. It must not be given to the subjects of Bright's disease.

    Perhaps the most valuable of all the medicinal applications of turpentine, and one which is rarely, if ever, mentioned in therapeutic textbooks — owing to the fact that gynaecology has been so extremely specialized — is in inoperable cancer of the uterus. Quite 90% of these cases are seen too late for operation, and nearly all recur after operation. The exhausting pain, the serious haemorrhages, and the abdominal septicity associated with a repulsive odour and the absorption of toxic products, which are the chief and ultimately fatal symptoms of that disease, are all directly combated by the administration of oil of turpentine. So beneficial is the action that for years there prevailed the unfortunately erroneous belief that Chian turpentine is actually curative in this condition. But it undoubtedly prolongs life, lessens suffering, and by checking the growth of bacteria upon the cancer reduces the fetid odour and the symptoms of septic intoxication.

    Old turpentine and French oil of turpentine are antidotes to phosphorus, forming turpentine-phosphoric acid, which is inert.

    Vitamin B1 (Thiamin)

    Vitamin B1, thiamin, was1 the first B vitamin to be discovered. Thiamin was2 originally thought to be an amine, the "e" was dropped when the formula became known. Severe thiamin deficiency can lead to wet beriberi, a cardiomyopathy with edema and fluid retention, gastrointestinal beriberi, an accumulation of lactate, dry beriberi, a peripheral neuropathy, and cerebral beriberi, a central nervous system disorder which can lead to Wernicke's encephalopathy or Wernicke-Korsakoff syndrome, also called alcohol dementia. People on a thiamin deficient diet are depleted within four weeks.

    Thiamin deficiency is most common in populations where polished rice and milled cereals are the primary food source, in alcoholics, and those with gastric bypass surgery or hyperthyroidism. The risk of deficiency increases with diuretic use, pregnancy, and lactation. People with sepsis require3 much more thiamin, in a study of septic shock alcoholics the death rate of those not given thiamin was 79%, versus 44% for those given 100 mg doses of thiamin.

    Good sources of thiamin include nutritional yeast, wheat germ, flaxseeds, hemp seeds, legumes (e.g., beans and lentils), nuts, and lean pork. Adults have an average dietary thiamin intake of 1.4 mg/day for men and 1.1 mg/day for women. Multivitamin supplements typically contain at least 1.2 mg of thiamin, the Daily Value (DV) for adults.

    Biology

    Thiamin catalyzes the generation of energy through decarboxylation of branched-chain amino acids and alpha-ketoacids, acts as a coenzyme for transketolase reactions in the form of thiamin pyrophosphate, and helps maintain the myelin sheath.

    Derivatives

    Thiamin is2 often found in supplements as the salts thiamin hydrochloride and thiamin mononitrate. Their absorption is poor, they can not get through the blood brain barrier, but sometimes they can help even with the poor absorption.

    Benfotiamine is a synthetic S-acyl lipid soluble derivative of thiamin that has a higher bioavailability than thiamin. It is not water soluble and can not get through the blood brain barrier, but it can help slightly more than thiamin salts.

    Allithiamin is a trade name for thiamin tetrahydrofurfuryl disulfide (TTFD). The prefix "alli" is from the allium species of plants, which includes garlic (allium sativum). Cell membranes have a lipid (fat) barrier, and allithiamin can get through this barrier, it also gets through the blood brain barrier. Because allithiamin is water soluble it can be given intravenously. Since it can get through cell membranes and the blood brain barrier it is the most effective form of thiamin to take, especially for dry beriberi which affects the central nervous system (CNS). Allithiamin requires4 glutathione, and vitamin B2 (riboflavin) to function safely. Glutathione synthesis requires cysteine, glutamate, glycine, selenium, magnesium and vitamin B6 (pyridoxine). The glutathione reductase enzyme also requires reducing power from nicotinamide adenine dinucleotide phosphate (NADPH). NADPH is derived from vitamin B3 (niacin) and is generated in the pentose phosphate pathway which requires the thiamin dependent enzyme transketolase. Allithiamin blocks5 taurine production causing a light-colored stool, so taurine is required. To safely take allithiamin, the patient should take a multivitamin with organic magnesium, a vitamin B supplement, taurine powder, and a glynac (a mixture of glycine and N-acetylcysteine (NAC)) supplement or a glycine supplement and a NAC supplement. Multivitamins which have magnesium in the form of magnesium oxide should never be taken because magnesium oxide has a low bioavailability. The B6 part of the supplement should preferably have regular niacin, not a time release form of niacin, like niacinamide or inositol hexanicotinate, because they might cause liver damage when used for a long time. The B9 part of the vitamin B supplement should be L-methylfolate (L-5-MTHF, (6S)-5-Methyltetrahydrofolic acid, Metafolin), not folic acid. The B12 part of the vitamin B supplement should be methylcobalamin and/or adenosylcobalamin (adenosyl B12, cobamamide, cobinamide). Hydroxocobalamin is unhealthy because it suppresses nitric oxide (NO). Cyanocobalamin depletes6 glutathione, might cause cyanide toxicity and should never be taken. Glycine and NAC provide the precursors for cells to make glutathione in the quantity they need, a study found7 that glynac improved cognition, strength, gait‐speed, exercise capacity and other attributes and biomarkers. For epileptics, glycine sometimes reduces8 the number of seizures, NAC attenuates aminophylline-induced seizures but aggravates9 absence seizures. So epileptics and others with hyperexcitable neurons should take a double dose of glycine instead of glynac or glycine and NAC separately. The taurine should be taken as a powder because the dose is typically around 2.5 grams/day, which is easier to take as a powder rather than a few capsules.

    Treatment

    Mild

    To treat a mild thiamin deficiency, it is best to start with a vitamin B supplement, with niacin (preferably not a time release form) and without cyanocobalamin, because they usually contain at least 10 mg of thiamin per dose, and the other B vitamins help the body use the thiamin. If this does not work, then add a thiamin supplement, they typically have 100 mg of thiamin. If this is not enough, use a benfotiamine supplement instead of the thiamin supplement, they typically have 100 mg of benfotiamine. If this is not enough, then treat it as a severe thiamin deficiency.

    Severe

    To treat a severe thiamin deficiency for people without hyperexcitable neurons, start with a vitamin B supplement, with niacin (preferably not a time release form) and without cyanocobalamin, if no adverse effects after three days add a multivitamin with organic magnesium, if no adverse effects after three more days add a glynac supplement or a glycine supplement and a NAC supplement, if no adverse effects after three more days add taurine powder, and if no adverse effects after three more days add an allithiamin supplement.

    To treat a severe thiamin deficiency for epileptics and other hyperexcitables, start with a vitamin B supplement, with niacin (preferably not a time release form) and without cyanocobalamin, if no adverse effects after three days add a multivitamin with organic magnesium, if no adverse effects after three more days add a double dose of a glycine supplement, if no adverse effects after three more days add taurine powder, and if no adverse effects after three more days add an allithiamin supplement.

    Critical

    Septic Shock

    The best treatment for septic shock is the Marik Protocol.

    To summarize, the Marik Protocol is standard Intensive Care Unit (ICU) care plus

    • Intravenous vitamin C 1.5 g, 4 times daily for 4 days or until ICU discharge
    • Intravenous hydrocortisone 50 mg, 4 times daily for 7 days or until ICU discharge, followed by a 3 day taper
    • Intravenous thiamin 200 mg, 2 times daily for 4 days or until ICU discharge

    The death rate with standard Intensive Care Unit (ICU) care is 40%. With the Marik Protocol, the mortality rate is 9%.

    Status Epilepticus

    When a drug for epilepsy is abruptly stopped, a dangerous state known as “status epilepticus” can occur. The epileptic seizure continues indefinitely and is difficult to interrupt, it may even be lethal. In this critical case, an intravenous injection of allithiamin should10 be given, it might stop the seizure.

    Deficiency

    Because thiamin deficiency can create wet beriberi, gastrointestinal beriberi, dry beriberi and cerebral beriberi, the symptoms can overlap.

    Symptoms - Wet Beriberi

    • Edema - Peripheral edema
    • Heart - Chest pain from demand ischemia
    • Heart - Dilated cardiomyopathy
    • Heart - High-output congestive heart failure
    • Heart - Tachycardia

    Symptoms - Gastrointestinal Beriberi

    • Abdominal - Severe abdominal pain
    • Lactic acidosis
    • Nausea - Nausea and vomiting

    Dry Beriberi and Cerebral Beriberi

    Dry beriberi is beriberi affecting the peripheral nervous system (PNS), and cerebral beriberi is beriberi affecting the central nervous system (CNS). Because the systems are closely related there is close overlap between these conditions. Cerebral beriberi may lead to Wernicke's encephalopathy or Wernicke-Korsakoff syndrome. Wernicke's disease is when amnesia is not present and Wernicke-Korsakoff syndrome (WKS) is when amnesia is present.

    Symptoms - Dry Beriberi
    • Extremities - Sensory deficits in the extremities
    • Myelin - Loss of myelin without acute inflammation
    • Neuropathy - Symmetric peripheral neuropathy
    • Reflexes - Diminished reflexes
    Symptoms - Wernicke Encephalopathy
    • Ataxia - Gait changes such as ataxia
    • Brain - Dizziness - Vertigo
    • Eye - Ocular abnormalities (horizontal nystagmus, ophthalmoplegia, double vision)
    • Fever
    • Mental - Confusion
    Symptoms - Wernicke-Korsakoff Syndrome
    • Brain - Psychosis - Epilepsy / Seizure
    • Memory - Memory loss
    • Mental - Apathy
    • Mental - Confabulation
    • Mental - Psychosis

    Vitamin B2 (Riboflavin)

    Vitamin B2 (riboflavin) is1 a water-soluble vitamin and antioxidant. The name riboflavin comes from the combination of ribose and flavin. Ribose is a sugar, known as D-ribose. Flavin is a pigment that gives riboflavin a bright yellow colour when it gets oxidized. Riboflavin is2 a coenzyme for glutathione reductase, which converts oxidized glutathione into its reduced form. Riboflavin helps digest and extract energy from foods by converting carbohydrates, fats and proteins into adenosine triphosphate (ATP). A riboflavin deficiency reduces the energy available, leading to energy deficiency problems including anaemia, fatigue, poor cognition, and sluggish metabolism. The recommended dietary allowance (RDA) for riboflavin is3 1.3 mg/day for men and 1.1 mg/day for women. No adverse effect of high riboflavin intake in humans is known.

    Biology

    Riboflavin is primarily found as part of the coenzymes flavin adenine dinucleotide (FAD) and flavin mononucleotide (FMN). Coenzymes derived from riboflavin are termed flavocoenzymes, and enzymes that use a flavocoenzyme are called flavoproteins. FAD and FMN act as electron carriers in a number of oxidation-reduction (redox) reactions involved in energy production. In conjunction with cytochrome P-450, flavocoenzymes also participate in the metabolism of drugs and toxins. Riboflavin is required for the metabolism of iron and vitamin B6 (pyridoxine), and in the synthesis of vitamin B3 (niacin) from tryptophan. It also plays an essential role in folate and related one-carbon metabolism, where FAD is required as a cofactor for methylenetetrahydrofolate reductase (MTHFR), a key folate-metabolizing enzyme. Glutathione reductase (GR) requires FAD to regenerate two molecules of reduced glutathione from oxidized glutathione. The conversion of vitamin B6 to its active coenzyme form in tissues, pyridoxal 5'-phosphate (PLP), requires the FMN-dependent enzyme, pyridoxine 5'-phosphate oxidase. Both FMN and FAD are coenzymes for the enzyme methionine synthase reductase, which regenerates methylcobalamin.

    Treatment

    About 10% of senior citizens in high income countries have evidence of riboflavin deficiency, also known as ariboflavinosis. Riboflavin deficiency is common in low and middle income countries. Riboflavin deficiency decreases conversion of vitamin B6 to its active coenzyme form (PLP) and conversion of tryptophan to niacin. A daily multivitamin usually provides at least 0.75 mg/day of riboflavin, which should be enough along with the diet to get adequate riboflavin. If someone has a riboflavin deficiency they should take a vitamin B supplement because the B vitamins work together and that person may have a deficiency of another B vitamin. The B6 part of the supplement should preferably have regular niacin, not a time release form of niacin, like niacinamide or inositol hexanicotinate, because they might cause liver damage when used for a long time. The B9 part of the vitamin B supplement should be L-methylfolate (L-5-MTHF, (6S)-5-Methyltetrahydrofolic acid, Metafolin), not folic acid. The B12 part of the vitamin B supplement should be methylcobalamin and/or adenosylcobalamin (adenosyl B12, cobamamide, cobinamide). Hydroxocobalamin is unhealthy because it suppresses nitric oxide (NO). Cyanocobalamin depletes4 glutathione, might cause cyanide toxicity and should never be taken.

    • Riboflavin metabolism disorder (Disorders of riboflavin metabolism) - Defective riboflavin transport-associated disorders (Brown-Vialetto-Van Laere syndrome 2 (BVVLS2) and Fazio Londe syndrome)24
    • Riboflavin metabolism disorder (Disorders of riboflavin metabolism) - Multiple acyl-CoA dehydrogenation deficiency (MADD) (Ethylmalonic/adipic acid syndrome) (Ethylmalonic-adipic aciduria)25
    • Skin - Low skin collagen12
    • Red blood cell - Sickle cell anemia26
    • Thyroid - Thyroid disease27

    Recoveries

    • Wound healing28

    Symptoms

    Symptoms of riboflavin deficiency3 follow below.

    • Eye - Blood vessels in the clear covering of the eye (vascularization of the cornea)
    • Lips - Cracks or sores on the outsides of the lips (cheliosis)
    • Mouth - Cracks or sores at the corners of the mouth (angular stomatitis)
    • Mouth and throat - Redness and swelling of the lining of the mouth and throat
    • Red blood cell - Decreased red blood cell count with normal hemoglobin and size (normochromic normocytic anemia)
    • Skin - Moist, scaly skin inflammation (seborrheic dermatitis)
    • Throat - Sore throat
    • Tongue - Inflammation and redness of the tongue (magenta tongue)

    Vitamin B3 (Niacin)

    Vitamin B3, niacin, is1 a water-soluble vitamin used by the body to form the nicotinamide coenzyme (NAD+). Niacin is often used to refer to nicotinic acid (pyridine-3-carboxylic acid) only, although other vitamers with a pyridine ring, including nicotinamide (pyridine-3-carboxamide) and nicotinamide riboside, also contribute to NAD+ formation.

    Pellagra is a disease of niacin deficiency, the word pellagra comes from "pelle agra," the Italian phrase for rough skin. The symptoms of pellagra are commonly sun-sensitive dermatitis, diarrhea, and delirium. Good sources of niacin include yeast, meat, poultry, red fish, fortified cereal, legumes, and seeds. In the United States, the average dietary intake of niacin is about 30 mg/day for young adult men and 20 mg/day for young adult women.

    Treatment

    A dose of 50 to 100 mg is2 enough to elicit flushing of the face, the rest of the body may be affected when doses of 500 to 1,000 mg are used. To lessen flushing, start3 with a lower dose, like 25 mg and gradually increase it. Also consuming niacin with food and/or plenty of water decreases the flushing. There are extended release forms of niacin which lessen of the flushing, however, these forms risk damaging the liver, so they should not be used.

    The Coronary Drug Project found4 that 3 g/day of niacin reduced mortality by 11%. This was mainly due to the reduction in coronary heart disease.

    Ailments

    High dose niacin, typically 3 g/day, can treat5 ailments which follow below.

    • Arthritis
    • Brain - Learning disorder
    • Brain - Memory disorder
    • Brain - Neurosis - Depression
    • Brain - Post traumatic stress disorder (PTSD)
    • Brain - Psychosis - Schizophrenia

    Recoveries

    • Alcoholicism recovery

    Bibliography

    1. Jane Higdon et al., Niacin - Linus Pauling Institute (2000)
    2. Linlin Ma et al., Nicotinic Acid Activates the Capsaicin Receptor TRPV1: Potential Mechanism for Cutaneous Flushing (March 2014)
    3. Stacy Facko, Why Does Niacin Cause Skin Flushing and Redness? (July 2024)
    4. Paul L. Canner et al., Fifteen Year Mortality in Coronary Drug Project Patients: Long-Term Benefit With Niacin (Dec. 1986)
    5. Abram Hoffer, Vitamin B-3: Niacin and Its Amide

    Vitamin C (Ascorbic Acid)

    Vitamin C, L-ascorbic acid, is1 the primary water-soluble, non-enzymatic antioxidant in plasma and tissues. It is2 a monosaccharide with the formula C6H8O6. A severe vitamin C deficiency causes scurvy1. A mild deficiency impairs the cardiovascular system, immune system, and the removal of lead.

    Biology

    Vitamin C also participates in redox recycling of other antioxidants, including vitamin E. Vitamin C is an essential cofactor in enzymatic reactions including the biosynthesis of collagen, carnitine, and neuropeptides.

    Forms

    Plant

    Oranges have3 about 53 mg of vitamin C per 100 g. Bell peppers have 128 mg of vitamin C per 100 g. The acerola cherry (Barbados cherry) has4 1.4 g of vitamin C per 100 g and the camu camu fruit has 2.1 g of vitamin C per 100 g. Boneset (break-bone fever, Eupatorium perfoliatum) is an herb rich in vitamin C. Acerola is rich in carotenoids, such as beta-carotene, beta-cryptoxanthin and lutein, which may cause problems for people with hypervitaminosis A. Boneset has5 potentially toxic pyrrolizidine alkaloids (PAs). Camu camu fruit has ellagic acid, which helps6 prevent cancer, obesity, wrinkles, collagen destruction and viral infections. Ellagic acid has no known adverse effects, so camu camu fruit is the healthiest concentrated plant source of vitamin C.

    Acid

    L-ascorbic acid is the most common supplemental form of vitamin C. Because it is acidic, some people get an upset stomach or diarrhea when taking ascorbic acid. Ascorbic acid has7 a two hour half life in blood serum, so ascorbic acid should be taken in divided doses.

    Salt

    Supplemental ascorbate salts include sodium ascorbate and calcium ascorbate. Sodium ascorbate has1 11% sodium and 89% ascorbate, calcium ascorbate has 10% calcium and 90% ascorbate. Compared to ascorbic acid, ascorbate salts have the advantage of being less likely to upset the stomach. However, because salts contain a metal, they should not be taken in megadoses because that would lead to a metal overdose. No more than 2 g/day of ascorbates should be taken, any vitamin C above that dose should be from ascorbic acid. If someone wants to take megadoses but gets an upset stomach from ascorbic acid, they should take any vitamin C above 2 g/day in liposomal form.

    Liposomal

    Vitamin C is water soluble and most does not get8 through the fatty acid cell membrane. Vitamin C has a bioavailability of about 20%. Liposomes are a globular double layer of fatty materials which carry nutrients in their interior. Liposome comes from the Greek words lipo (fat) and soma (body). Liposomes penetrate the fatty cell membrane, and liposomal vitamin C has a bioavailability of over 90%. The half life of blood serum vitamin C after taking liposomal vitamin C is about 2.5 hours, so liposomal vitamin C should be taken in divided doses. A healthy carrier for liposomal vitamin C is phosphatidyl choline (PC) from non-GMO sunflower lecithin. Liposomes should be around 250 nm in diameter.

    Liposomal vitamin C can be made at home with ascorbic acid, phosphatidyl choline (PC) from non-GMO sunflower lecithin granules, 40% ethyl alcohol or spirit, distilled water, an ultrasonic cleaner, a blender, a beaker, a stirring spoon, a scale, a thermometer and a quart wide mouth jar. Lecithin granules should be used instead of liquid lecithin because the granules are higher in phosphatidylcholine. 40% ethyl alcohol or spirit are recommended instead of USP grade alcohol because USP alcohol is almost always denatured. The ultrasonic cleaner should have a symmetric tank, for example in the shape of a square or circle, a stack transducer with at least 50 W of power, and a holder for a beaker. The beaker should be made of glass and is necessary to keep the choline away from the tank to avoid corrosion of the stainless steel from the acidic vitamin C, to prevent contamination of the product and for easier cleaning. The ethyl alcohol is a solvent and helps the phospholipids form liposomes, and it preserves them once they are made. The stirring spoon should be wooden or plastic, preferably wooden. The quart wide mouth jar should be made of glass. Containers should be glass if possible, and if not stainless steel, plastic is the worst because some plastic will get into the product.

    A summary of instructions to make9 liposomal vitamin C for a one liter beaker follows below. The summary is incomplete and should only be used as an overview if the original instructions are no longer available. The encapsulation degrades above 35°C, so if the temperature reaches 35°C as a result of blending or ultrasound, put the beaker in the fridge for an hour to cool it, then continue the process.

    • Stirring in the beaker with ultrasound, dissolve 161 g of vitamin C in 255 g distilled water and 338 g of 40% alcohol
    • Transfer to the blender, add 99 g of lecithin granules and blend, then add the remaining 99 g of granules and blend
    • Transfer to the beaker, cover with a plastic wrap, and degas the mixture with ultrasound for 30 minutes or until bubbles are removed
    • Alternate ultrasound and refrigeration three times to encapsulate more ascorbic acid
    • Skim the bubbles off the top of the mixture then pour into a glass jar

    Human Vitamin C Synthesis

    Most other animals synthesize vitamin C throughout their lives. Humans synthesize vitamin C before they are10 born and usually for at least six months after. Most adults need vitamin C from food, however some do not. It is not known if the few adults who do not need vitamin C from food are synthesizing their own or if it is being synthesized by their gut microbiota. The vitamin C synthesis pathway is D-glucose to D-glucuronic acid to L-gulonic acid to L-gulonolactone to L-ascorbic acid. Before they are born humans produce the L-gulonolactone oxidase (GULO) enzyme, which converts L-gulonolactone to L-ascorbic acid, and GULO is also produced in most adults who take 45 mg/day of hydroxytyrosol (HT). Hydroxytyrosol is a polyphenol found in olive mill waste and virgin olive oil. After taking hydroxytyrosol for a week, vitamin C blood levels typically increase by between 50% and 200%. When people take hydroxytyrosol, the synthesis of vitamin C increases when there is a greater need, for example when drinking alcohol.

    Megadose

    Main article: Vitamin C (Ascorbic Acid) - Megadose

    Ascorbyl Phosphate

    Ascorbyl phosphate, ascorbic acid 2-phosphate (ASC2P), L-ascorbic acid 2-phosphate, Asc-2-O-phosphate, is an autooxidation-resistant derivative of ascorbic acid. It slows11 the shortening of telomeric DNA. The telomere study was in vitro, it is not known how much to take to protect human telomeres. This compound is part of the supplement magnesium ascorbyl phosphate.

    Treatment - Deficiency

    The requirement to prevent scurvy is 10 mg/day. The recommended minumum daily intake for men who smoke is 125 mg/day.

    Ailment

    • Scurvy1

    Treatment - Supplementation

    The amount of vitamin C required to prevent chronic disease is higher than the minumum daily intake. The more vitamin C people take, up to about 10 g/day, the healthier they will be. Because vitamin C has7 a two hour half life in blood serum, vitamin C should be taken in divided doses over the day. Many of the health benefits are obtained at 400 mg/day of vitamin C. Going to 2 g/day will give some additional benefit with a low risk of adverse effects. Above 2 g/day, people might get diarrhea and/or gastrointestinal disturbances. If a person is sick, their vitamin C requirement increases.

    Ailments

    • Arthritis - Gout (Inflammatory arthritis)1
    • Brain - Headache - Headache pain (Migraine pain)12
    • Brain - Psychosis - Schizophrenia13
    • Burns - Sunburn14
    • Cardiovascular - Angina (Angina pectoris)15 16
    • Cardiovascular - Cardiovascular disease1 17
    • Cardiovascular - Endothelial dysfunction1
    • Cardiovascular - Hypertension (High blood pressure)1

    • Placental abruption1
    • Postoperative problems14
    • Pregnancy disorder14
    • Preterm birth1
    • Respiratory disease - Asthma19
    • Skin - Poison oak or ivy rash13
    • Skin - Stretch marks (Striae gravidarum)13
    • Toxicity - Lead toxicity1
    • Urethra - Urethritis13
    • Viral infection - Common cold20

    Treatment - Critical

    Ailment - Angina

    Angina, narrowing of the arteries in general, and thrombosis are15 16 caused by plaque. Lysyl hydroxylase is an enzyme responsible for connecting lysine residues on adjacent collagen strands. Lysyl hydroxylase requires vitamin C, a vitamin C deficiency leads to insufficient lysyl hydroxylase, which disrupts lysine crosslinking, which weakens collagen strands. When collagen is weak it cracks, and if there is a lysine and/or proline deficiency, the exposed lysine strands from the crack bind to circulating lipoprotein (a), a cholesterol that has lysine receptors. The attachment of lipoprotein(a) to the free lysine residues of damaged collagen builds plaque deposits which eventually narrow the artery obstructing blood flow, or the plaques rupture leading to thrombosis, a blood clot inside a blood vessel, which also obstructs blood flow.

    The standard Pauling Protocol to treat angina is 3 g of vitamin C, 2.5 g of lysine, and 1.25 g of proline, taken twice daily with food. The total dose per day is 6 g of vitamin C, 5 g of lysine, and 2.5 g of proline. Also, 300 mg of annatto vitamin E should be taken once per day. The fast Pauling Protocol to treat angina quickly is 2 g of vitamin C, 2 g of lysine, 1 g of proline, taken twice daily away from food. The total dose per day is 4 g of vitamin C, 4 g of lysine, and 2 g of proline. Also, 300 mg of annatto vitamin E should be taken once per day.

    Ailment - Septic Shock

    The best treatment for septic shock is the Marik Protocol.

    To summarize, the Marik Protocol is standard Intensive Care Unit (ICU) care plus

    • Intravenous vitamin C 1.5 g, 4 times daily for 4 days or until ICU discharge
    • Intravenous hydrocortisone 50 mg, 4 times daily for 7 days or until ICU discharge, followed by a 3 day taper
    • Intravenous thiamin 200 mg, 2 times daily for 4 days or until ICU discharge

    The death rate with standard Intensive Care Unit (ICU) care is 40%. With the Marik Protocol, the mortality rate is 9%.

    Vitamin C (Ascorbic Acid) - Megadose

    Forms

    Intravenous Megadose

    With megadoses of vitamin C, usually from 30 to 200 g/day, it is1 mostly thrown away for the reducing equivalents it carries. With these doses it is possible to saturate the body with reducing equivalents, neutralize the excessive free radicals, and drive a reducing redox potential into involved tissues. Inflammations mediated by free radicals are reduced. Often patients with autoimmune disease have their humeral immunity controlled while their cellular immunity is augmented. To the extent that free radicals are either essential to the perpetuation of a disease or just part of the symptoms, the disease will be cured or just ameliorated.

    The sodium ascorbate used2 intravenously and intramuscularly must not contain preservatives. There is usually a small amount of EDTA in the preparation to chelate trace amounts of copper and iron which might destroy the ascorbate. Solutions containing sodium ascorbate 250 or 500 mg/cc can be obtained. The 250 mg/cc solutions may be used in young children intramuscularly in doses usually 350 mg/kg body weight up to every 2 hours. If the volume of the material becomes too great for intramuscular injections, then the intravenous route should be used. Inadequate doses will be ineffective. Quite frequently a child initially refusing oral ascorbate will cooperate after injections if given the alternative. These intramuscular injections can be used in a crisis situation. Kalokerinos describes cases where certain death in infants in shock has been averted by emergency intramuscular ascorbate.

    For intravenous solutions concentrations of 60 g/l are made with the 250 or 500 mg/cc sodium ascorbate diluted with Ringer's lactate. Ascorbate is more efficient intravenously than orally in part because gastrointestinal processes break down some of the ascorbate. Doses of 400 to 700 mg/kg of body weight per 24 hours usually suffice. Rate of infusion can be determined by ensuring that symptoms are suppressed and that the patient not become dehydrated or receive sodium too rapidly. Local soreness in the vein caused by too rapid infusion is relieved by slowing the infusion. At least one gram of calcium gluconate must be added to the bottles each day to prevent tetany by replacing calcium ions removed in the breakdown chemical action as ascorbic acid goes to dehydroascorbic acid, then to ketogulonic acid and later to oxalic acid as the calcium salt.

    The maximum relief of symptoms which can be expected with oral doses of ascorbic acid is obtained at a point just short of the amount which produces diarrhea. The amount and the timing of the doses are usually sensed by the patient. The physician should not try to regulate exactly the amount and timing of these doses because the optimally effective dose will often change from dose to dose. Patients are instructed on the general principles of determining doses and given estimates of the reasonable starting amounts and timing of these doses. The process of the patient determining the optimum dose is called titrating to bowel tolerance. The patient tries to titrate between that amount which begins to make her feel better and that which almost but not quite causes diarrhea.

    Patients frequently underdose themselves and need professional guidance to push the doses to effective levels. Some people, more frequently the elderly, are intolerant to oral doses but are able to tolerate intravenous ascorbate. Patients with severe problems may need to be treated intravenously if very high doses are maintained for a long time to suppress the symptoms. A typical starting dose schedule for various weights follows3 below.

    Oral Megadose

    To achieve high vitamin C activity with oral supplementation, vitamin C should be taken away from carbohydrates because vitamin C absorption is impaired by carbohydrates via glucose competition. Liposomal vitamin C should also be taken. Alpha-lipoic acid should also be taken because it increases4 the conversion of dehydroascorbic acid to ascorbic acid. It is not known how effective oral megadosing with these three supplements away from carbohydrates is compared to intravenous administration, but it's worth trying if intravenous administration is not available or desired.

    Ailments - Bacterial Infections

    Megadoses of intravenous vitamin C along with antibiotics will usually cure a bacterial infection. The vitamin C enables a cure with smaller doses of antibiotics, while reducing the adverse effects of antibiotics. Infections that megadoses of vitamin C have cured follow below.

    • Bacterial infection - Croupous pneumonia5
    • Bacterial infection - Diphtheria6
    • Bacterial infection - Dysentery5
    • Bacterial infection - Leprosy5
    • Bacterial infection - Lyme disease7
    • Bacterial infection - Pertussis (Whooping cough)5
    • Bacterial infection - Pseudomonas8
    • Bacterial infection - Tuberculosis5
    • Bacterial infection - Typhoid fever5

    Ailments - Cancer

    Megadoses of intravenous vitamin C may cure cancer. There is only one report of this being tried. The patient had two cancers which follow below.

    • Cancer - Leukemia9
    • Cancer - Polycythemia9

    Ailments - Miscellaneous

    Miscellaneous problems that megadoses of vitamin C have helped with follow below.

    Ailments - Parasitic Infections

    Megadoses of intravenous vitamin C may cure some parasitic infections. There is only one report of this being tried.

    • Parasitic infection - Trichinosis6

    Ailments - Toxins

    A megadose vitamin C injection is necessary to save a victim of a toxic bite, including a bite from a scorpion, or a bite from a cobra, copperhead, coral, moccasin, or rattler snake, or a bite from a black widow or fiddle spider. If a victim is bitten by an unknown animal, a megadose vitamin C injection should be performed immediately because there is no other antitoxin that counters as many types of toxins as vitamin C. Carbon monoxide poisoning also requires a megadose vitamin C injection. For acute pesticide poisoning a megadose vitamin C injection will work and oral vitamin C might work. For metal poisoning, oral vitamin C is sufficient.

    • Bites - Moccasin bite6
    • Bites - Puss caterpillar bite6
    • Bites - Scorpion bite11
    • Bites - Unknown snake bite11

    • Poisoning - Alcohol intoxication (Ethanol intoxication)- Alcohol poisoning6

    Ailments - Viral Infections

    Megadoses of intravenous vitamin C will almost always cure a viral infection. If a patient has an agressive unknown virus, a megadose vitamin C injection should be performed immediately because there is no other antiviral that counters as many types of viruses as vitamin C. Viral infections that megadoses of vitamin C have cured follow below.

    11. Irwin Stone, The Healing Factor - Vitamin C Against Disease - Chapter 24 - Chemical Stresses - Poisons, Toxins (1972)
    12. Irwin Stone, The Healing Factor - Vitamin C Against Disease - Chapter 13 - Viral Infection (1972)
    13. Irwin Stone, The Healing Factor - Vitamin C Against Disease - Chapter 12 - The Common Cold (1972)

    Vitamin D3

    Vitamin D2 (ergocalciferol) has1 the formula C28H44O, vitamin D3 (cholecalciferol) has the formula C27H44O. Vitamin D3 is produced in the skin of vertebrates, where it is formed2 by the action of ultraviolet B (UVB) light (290 - 320 nm) on 7-dehydrocholesterol. Vitamin D2 has been found in some mushrooms, where it is formed by UVB light on ergosterol. Vitamin D3 is present in animal foods such as eggs, fish and liver, and in small amounts in meat.

    Most people in summer get 50% to 90% of their vitamin D3 via exposure of the skin to UVB through sunlight exposure. However, those people who stay indoors in summer, or always wear sunscreen, or wear head to toe clothing, won't get much vitamin D3 from sunlight. In winter, oral intake of vitamin D3 is usually the primary source.

    History

    The United Kingdom, and especially Scotland, United Kingdom, had a high incidence of rickets. Edward Melany hypothesised that this was due to a dietary deficiency, to test this he fed dogs the diet consumed in Scotland, primarily oatmeal, kept them away from sunlight and they also developed rickets. He then fed them cod liver oil, which cured the rickets. Melany hypothesised that this was because of the vitamin A in the oil, McCollum then tested this hypothesis by destroying the vitamin A in the oil by bubbling oxygen through it. The oil without vitamin A still retained the ability to cure rickets, so he and Melany concluded that the oil had another vitamin which they named vitamin D.

    Treatment

    Vitamin D2 potency is less3 than one third that of vitamin D3, so supplementation should only be done with vitamin D3. Taking vitamin D3 without vitamin K2 leads4 to high levels of circulating calcium, which increases calcium accumulation in blood vessel walls, which leads to arterial plaque formation and then to cardiovascular disease. Vitamin K2 directs calcium from the blood into bones, which balances blood calcium levels and decreases soft tissue calcification. Therefore, people should supplement with vitamin K2, especially when supplementing with vitamin D3. The optimal dose vitamin D3 dose for disease prevention is5 4,000 IU/day. The typical vitamin K2 dose is6 around 70 mcg/day of MK-7 or 1,500 mcg/day of MK-4.

    Ailments

    Vitamin D3 improves7 bone health by increasing calcium absorption, stimulating bone maturation, matrix formation, renal reabsorption of calcium, bone remodeling and osteoclast cell activity. Ailments which it helps with follow below.

    • Bone - Osteoporosis
    • Cancer
    • Neurodegenerative disease - Multiple sclerosis (MS)

    Bibliography

    Vitamin E

    Vitamin E is a fat-soluble antioxidant. Vitamin E resides1 within the lipid cell membrane to protect its integrity. Vitamin E has a chromanol head with a lipid-soluble side chain. This nutrient is only found2 in plants, including annatto, almonds, peanuts, sunflower seeds, mangoes, avocadoes, asparagus, bell peppers, collard greens and spinach. The typical dietary consumption is3 about 20 mg/day. Using the factor (0.8) from NHANES III data to adjust for α-tocopherol equivalents, the intake equates to 16 mg/day of α-tocopherol.

    Biology

    Vitamin E comes in two groups, the tocopherol group which has a saturated sidechain in the tail of the molecule and the tocotrienol group which has4 an unsaturated sidechain. The tocotrienol unsaturated sidechain is shorter than the tocopherol saturated sidechain, and the shortened sidechain increases tocotrienol's flexibility which increases its movement speed in cell membranes by about 50 times over tocopherol. Each of these two groups has four members, the alpha, beta, gamma and delta. The alpha form has the largest head, the delta form has the smallest head, and the beta and gamma are in between. It is easier for smaller molecules to access the cell membrane, and smaller molecules are more active. So delta-tocotrienol, the smallest of the eight vitamin E forms, is the most effective cell membrane antioxidant. Annatto has the highest concentration of delta-tocotrienol of any plant.

    Nonalcoholic Fatty Liver Disease

    In a six month study with 71 patients, compared to the 35 placebo patients, the 36 patients who received 600 mg/day of annatto tocotrienol lowered5 their fatty liver index (FLI) by 8.5, their homeostasis model of insulin resistance (HOMA-IR) by 0.37, their hs-CRP by 0.61, their malondialdehyde (MDA) by 0.91, their alanine transaminase (ALT) by 8.9, and their aspartate transaminase (AST) by 6.6.

    Osteopenia

    In a three month study with eighty-nine postmenopausal osteopenic women, the patients were given either a placebo, 430 mg/day of annatto tocotrienol, or 860 mg/day of annatto tocotrienol. Measurements were6 made of the levels of bone markers including cross-linked N-telopeptides of bone type I collagen (NTx) in the urine. The amount of NTx in the blood is used to assess the amount of bone breakdown, this decreased in the patients who received annatto tocotrienol, by a similar amount in the medium dose group and in the high dose group. So taking 430 mg/day is enough to slow bone breakdown, which would increase the bone density.

    Treatment

    Annatto tocotrienol is the best form of Vitamin E to take, the optimal dose to lower total cholesterol and triglycerides is7 250 mg/day, and it should be taken with a meal.

    Ailments

    Annatto tocotrienol also helps8 maintain healthy eyesight, supports healthy skin, and reduces oxidative stress. Ailments which it helps with follow below.

    • Bone - Osteopenia6
    • Cardiovascular - Cardiovascular disease8
    • Diabetes - Hyperglycemia (High blood sugar)8
    • Eye - Poor eyesight8
    • Liver - Nonalcoholic Fatty Liver Disease (NAFLD)5
    • Skin - Poor skin8

    Vitamin K2

    When Carl Peter Henrik Dam was studying1 cholesterol metabolism from 1928 to 1930, he observed a tendency to hemorrhage in chicks fed for longer than a few weeks on feed without cholesterol or fat. Since no other vitamin was antihaemorrhagic, he postulated a new, fat-soluble vitamin, which he called vitamin K (after Koagulation in German).

    K vitamins include vitamin K1, phylloquinone (2-methyl-3-phytyl-1,4-naphthoquinone, phytomenadione), which is contained in green plants and vitamin K2, menaquinone, with side chains of varying length, which is formed from intestinal bacteria (e.g., Bacteroides). Menaquinones are mainly found in foods of animal origin, such as bovine liver and in fermented foods, including yogurt and some cheeses. The menaquinones are called MK-n, where n signifies the number of isoprenoid units. Menaquinone-4 (MK-4) and menaquinone-7 (MK-7) are common. The richest source of MK-7 at 10 μg/g is natto, which is made from fermented soya beans by the bacterium Bacillus subtilis natto.

    Vitamin K2 is necessary to move calcium from places it does not belong, like arteries, to places where it does belong, like bones and teeth, making bones strong and teeth resistant to cavities. Only vitamin K2 does this, vitamin K1 does not. Vitamin K2 in supplements is usually in the MK-7 or MK-4 form. To noticeably carboxylate osteocalcin requires2 1,500 mcg/day of MK-4 or 45 to 90 mcg/day of MK-7, so MK-7 is roughly 22 times more effective.

    Treatment

    The typical dose for MK-7 is 45 to 120 mcg/day, and the typical dose for MK-4 is 1,500 mcg/day (1.5 mg/day). If the supplement does not say what type it is, then don't take it because there's no way to know if it has enough vitamin K2 to be effective.

    Ailments

    Vitamin K2 helps with ailments which follow below.

    • Bone - Bone fractures3
    • Bone - Osteoporosis4
    • Cancer - Prostate cancer5
    • Cardiovascular - Arterial calcification6
    • Cardiovascular - Arteriosclerosis7
    • Diabetes - Diabetes Type II8
    • Heart - Coronary heart disease7

    Bibliography

    2. CanPrev, What form of vitamin K2 should I take?
    3. P Szulc et al., Serum undercarboxylated osteocalcin is a marker of the risk of hip fracture in elderly women (1993 April)
    4. M H J Knapen et al., Three-year low-dose menaquinone-7 supplementation helps decrease bone loss in healthy postmenopausal women (2013 Sep.)

    8. Joline W J Beulens et al., Dietary phylloquinone and menaquinones intakes and risk of type 2 diabetes (2010 Aug.)

    Water Filter

    Water can be contaminated with toxic metals, bacteria, parasites, viruses, microplastics, volatile organic contaminants (VOCs), pesticides, herbicides, per- and polyfluoroalkyl substances (PFAS) and pharmaceuticals. Bacteria, parasites and microplastics are much larger than molecules, so they are easy to filter out and almost every water filter will remove those. Only a few water filter elements will remove toxic metals including aluminum, these include the Black Berkey1 filters, CF108W Coldstream CTO Plus2 filters, CF163W Coldstream FTO Plus3 filters, and CF504W Coldstream Max4 filters. The only water filters worth buying are those which have test reports showing the removal of at least 80% of aluminum, arsenic, cadmium, lead, mercury and thallium.

    Bottled water which does not come in glass or stainless steel bottles should be put through a water filter before use, because it will have microplastics. When water is transported, it should be in glass or stainless steel bottles.

    Toxic Metals

    Aluminum

    Aluminium is5 a neurotoxin, it is6 the primary cause of Alzheimer's disease. Aluminum also increases the chance of getting other neurological diseases including7 autism and attention deficit hyperactivity disorder (ADHD). Lysosomes are cytoplasmatic organelles which use to keep their interiors acidic, to break down garbage in the body which is then recyled or excreted. Aluminum inhibits8 lysosomal proton pumps, leading to the accumulation of cellular garbage in the body. Some of this garbage is flagged by the immune system as foreign material, so the immune system then attacks it, which can lead to autoimmune ailments. The garbage includes cholesterol containg lipid particles that are taken up into plaque, causing heart disease. Glutathione is a detoxifier and the body's master antioxidant. Aluminum decreases9 the regeneration of glutathione from the oxidized form by inhibiting NADP-isocitrate dehydrogenase, which supplies NADPH in mitochondria.

    Ailments
    • Brain - Dementia - Alzheimer's disease6
    • Brain - Neurodevelopmental disorder - Attention deficit/hyperactivity disorder (ADHD)7
    • Brain - Neurodevelopmental disorder - Autism7
    • Cardiovascular - Atherosclerotic plaque8
    • Immune dysfunction - Autoimmune disease8
    • Mitochondrial dsyfunction9

    Arsenic

    Arsenic increases the risk of diabetes partly because of its propensity to form10 trivalent metabolites, which inhibit the synthesis of insulin. Arsenic increases11 generation of atherosclerotic plaque in the arteries, in part because of inflammation from reactive nitrogen species generation. The higher12 the exposure to arsenic, the thicker the Carotid intima-media thickness (cIMT), which is associated with arterial problems. Also, arsenic prolongs13 the QTc interval.

    Ailments
    • Diabetes10
    • Cardiovascular - Atherosclerotic plaque11
    • Cardiovascular - Arterial wall thickening (Thickening of arterial walls)12
    • Heart - Long QT interval (Prolonged QTc interval)13

    Cadmium

    Cardiomyocytes are the major type of cells that form the heart. Cadmium inhibits14 cardiomyocyte differentiation and cardiac induction, increasing the chance of congenital heart disease (CHD). Cadmium leads15 to peripheral artery disease.

    Cadmium sources include16 mining, combustion emissions, and cadmium containing fertilizers. Cadmium is also incorporated into sulfides, carbonates, and phosphorites resulting in elevated cadmium concentrations in associated rock types. Weathering can lead to cadmium concentrations up to 5 mcg/L in soil water and up to 1 mcg/L in groundwater.

    Ailments
    • Cardiovascular - Peripheral artery disease (Peripheral arterial disease) (PAD) (Arterial insufficiency of the peripheral circulation)14
    • Heart - Congenital heart disease (CHD)14

    Lead

    Lead damages17 the endothelial cells that line blood vessels. This hardens arteries and causes plaque to form. Lead increases18 blood pressure, in part by disturbing the calcium messenger system regulation of blood pressure. Lead is found in the soil because of past use of leaded gasoline, water can have lead because old plumbing solder used lead, old paint sometimes has lead.

    Ailments
    • Cardiovascular - Atherosclerotic plaque17
    • Cardiovascular - Hypertension (High blood pressure)18

    Mercury

    Mercury is used in gold amalgamation processes and the concentration of mercury in people and seafood in a gold mining area were19 measured. The most frequent symptoms documented were headache, muscle cramps, cough, and aphthous ulcers. Sometimes there is a delay between exposure to methylmercury and the onset20 of neurodegenerative symptoms. Mercury increases21 production of free radicals and also disables antioxidant defenses, including22 glutathione.

    Mercury activates23 the enzyme phospholipase D (PLD). The enzyme in turn triggers the release of phosphatidic acid, which damages endothelial cells in the blood vessel lining, which leads to vascular disorders. Mercury induces thrombosis, partly by changing the shape of platelets. Mercury induced inflammation alters24 arachidonic acid metabolites, increasing the porosity of the vascular endothelium. Vascular smooth muscle cells (VSMCs) help regulate blood pressure, mercury alters them and therefore increases the risk of hypertension. Mercury induces dyslipidemia, immune dsyfunction and mitochondrial dsyfunction.

    Ailments
    • Brain - Headache19
    • Cardiovascular - Dyslipidemia24
    • Cardiovascular - Hypertension (High blood pressure)24
    • Cardiovascular - Thrombosis23
    • Immune dysfunction24
    • Mitochondrial dsyfunction24
    • Musculoskeletal - Muscle cramps19
    • Ulcer - Aphthous ulcers19
    • Vascular disorders23

    Thallium

    Thallium causes25 oxidative stress and produces Reactive Oxygen Species (ROS), which lead to heart disease. Thallium passes across the blood brain barrier and accumulates in the brain with lipid oxidation products. Thallium causes swelling and apoptosis resulting from the opening of the mitochondrial permeability transition (MPT) pore

    Ailment
    • Heart - Heart disease25

    Pathogens

    Water borne bacteria include26 escherichia coli, campylobacter jejuni, giardia lamblia, salmonella, legionella pneumophila, and cryptosporidium. Water borne parasites include entamoeba histolytica, naegleria spp, toxoplasma gondii, isospora belli, balantidium coli, acanthamoeba spp, sarcocystis spp, cyclospora cayetanensis. Water borne viruses include norovirus, adenovirus, hepatitis A and E viruses, astrovirus, rotavirus. Pathogens are more common in untreated water sources.

    Microplastics

    Microplastics in water have27 harmful effects including disrupted hormone function, neurotoxicity, carcinogenic effects, weight gain, poor fetal brain development, and allergic reactions. Microplastics get into water from surface runoff, sewer overflows, wastewater, and the air. Surface water has a higher concentration of microplastics than groundwater.

    Toxic Compounds

    VOCs in water include28 perchloroethylene (PCE), trihalomethanes (THMs), methyl tert-butyl ether (MTBE) and chlorobenzene. VOCs are organic chemicals with low boiling points, they can cause cancer, dizziness, kidney and liver damage.

    Pesticides and herbicides include29 2,4-dichlorophenoxyacetic acid (2,4-D), atrazine, carbofuran, chlordane and dalapon. They get into water sources by surface runoff, and can cause nervous system damage, cancer, skin and eye irritation, and hormone and/or endocrine system disruption.

    Per- and polyfluoroalkyl substances (PFAS) are30 synthetic chemicals with carbon fluorine bonds. They are known as forever chemicals because they break down very slowly and therefore bioaccumulate. PFAS can reduce resistance to infectious disease, cause cancer, increase the risk of premature births, lower birth weight, reduce the chance of getting pregnant, impair the thyroid, and increase cholesterol.

    Pharmaceutically active micropollutants (PhAMP) are found31 in wastewater, surface water bodies, and groundwater. Pharmaceuticals found in high concentrations in wastewater include non-steroidal anti-inflammatory drugs (NSAIDs), beta-blockers, psychoactive compounds, analgesics, antibiotics, endocrine disruptors, antiretroviral drugs, and drugs to treat cancer. Of these micropollutants, the most studied are endocrine disruptors, which increase the risk of reproductive problems, Alzheimer’s disease, thyroid problems, obesity32 and prostate, breast or endometrium cancer.

    Zinc

    Zinc, a metallic chemical element; its symbol is Zn, and atomic weight 65.37 (O=16). Zinc as a component of brass (χαλκός, όρεί-χαλκος) had currency in metallurgy long before it became known as an individual metal. Aristotle refers to brass as the "metal of the Mosynoeci," which is produced as a bright and light coloured xahifa, not by addition of tin, but by fusing up with an earth.

    Compounds

    Zinc Orotate

    Treatment
    Ailments

    Zinc orotate stabilizes1 blood glucose and reduces the need for insulin in diabetics, according to Hans Nieper. Zinc orotate and other zinc compounds work with sulfur-containing antioxidants (sulfhydryls) to protect against free radical-induced tissue injury. Zinc orotate should treat every ailment that other zinc compounds treat with fewer adverse effects, but this has not been tested for most ailments because the other compounds are more popular.

    • Diabetes - Hyperglycemia (High blood sugar)
    • Free radical-induced tissue injury

    Bibliography

    1. Loretta Lanphier, Orotates and Mineral Transporters – Fact or Fiction (2018 Aug.)
